Igor: I promised Urd the operation would go smoothly, but I lied. Neither Zeno nor the Foundation had any idea how powerful the Manus's defensive ritual was.

伊戈尔：情况过于危急，所有战斗人员都只得到了一条命令——前进，不计伤亡。
Igor: The situation was desperate. We had only one order: advance, regardless of the casualties.

伊戈尔：战役的细节被“暴雨”带走，只剩沉重的情绪还留在我的回忆中，那是下令让无数士兵走向死亡的悲痛。
Igor: When the "Storm" rose, it swallowed the details of the war. Yet the weight of it haunts me still—the grief of sending my soldiers to die.

伊戈尔：无数性命像酒杯口的小虫子一样，轻易地滑向了深渊，再也没有回来。
Igor: Like the flame of a candle, they were extinguished in an instant.

伊戈尔：如果不是被第一场“暴雨”或多或少带走了记忆，我离开芝诺与基金会的时间只会更早。
Igor: If it weren't for the "Storm" blurring my memories, I would've left Zeno and the Foundation far sooner.

地铁站走到了尽头，前面似乎是一个更广阔的地带，白色的光线和风灌了进来。
The subway station ends, and ahead of them lies a broader space, where white light and air pour in.

维尔汀：那之后又是什么导致了你背叛芝诺和基金会？
Vertin: Then, what ultimately led to your betrayal?

将军停下了脚步，看向大厅角落不起眼的门。
Igor halts and turns toward an obscure door at the corner of the hall.

伊戈尔：——我们到了。
Igor: We've arrived.

它和墙壁是一样光滑的大理石，需要仔细看才能辨认出轮廓。但从视线停在门上的那一刻起，所有人都感觉得到其神秘。
It's carved from the same smooth marble as the surrounding wall, its outline only perceptible on close inspection. Unobtrusive, unremarkable even, but ever so mysterious.

伊戈尔：……正是琥珀屋项目让我想起了鸽子屋治下一切的傲慢。
Igor: It was the Amber Room Project. It showed me the Pax House's arrogance.

伊戈尔：我不清楚，在对生命的漠视方面，基金会和重塑之手究竟谁更加令人绝望。
Igor: By now, I don't know which shows less respect for life, the Foundation or Manus Vindictae.

伊戈尔：我曾以为，我们的战斗和牺牲都建立在充足的理由与信念上，都是为了一个和平而美好的未来。
Igor: I once thought that we fought and sacrificed for a firm conviction, to bring a bright and peaceful future.

伊戈尔：但在见过这一切之后，我很难再欺骗自己。我知道鸽子屋在缔造属于人类与神秘学家共同的和平，但我已不再相信他们的路径。
Igor: But I can fool myself no longer. The Pax House may aim to build a peaceful future for both humans and arcanists, but their means are no longer justifiable.

伊戈尔：而且……阿尔卡纳的存在让我意识到，这是一场属于神明的战争，作为凡人，我不知道如何取胜。
Igor: And, with Arcana as She is, this is a war for gods. How can we stand—let alone claim victory—as mere mortals?

伊戈尔：我希望，也有一位神明能站在自己这边，司辰。
Igor: How I wish to have a god on my side, Timekeeper.

他的态度几近恳求。
There is an almost pleading note in his voice.

伊戈尔：或许是实验的全部资料，或许只是兀尔德女士留给你的只言片语。我不知道这里面具体有什么，但我知道这是她希望留给你的东西。
Igor: What lies in the Amber Room, I cannot fully say. Data fragments, Ms. Urd's words, whatever it is, she wants you to have it.

伊戈尔：因“命运”的力量，它们得以在“暴雨”中长存，只是为了等待你的到来。我想，你应该接受它。
Igor: Destiny has seen it survive several "Storms," waiting for this hour, for you.

伊戈尔：穿过这扇门。这是只有你与兀尔德女士能打开的门。
Igor: This is a door only you and Ms. Urd may open. Go. Walk through it.

维尔汀：……我不能确定你说的一切是否属实，不过，谢谢你能带我到这里，伊戈尔。
Vertin: I'm still not sure if you're telling the truth, but thank you for bringing me here, Igor.

12TH-11 赫克托耳宣言 / The Defender's Oath

实验人员：兀尔德女士，你感觉如何？
Laboratory Technician: How are you feeling, Ms. Urd?

兀尔德？：和之前的每一次一样，这张椅子我已经坐上去过很多次了。另外，你们一定要用我的笔名来称呼我吗？
Urd?: Just as I have the many other times I've sat on this chair. And must you insist on calling me by my pen name?

实验人员：那才是属于你的名字。你想要找回你自己，那首先就要接受它。
Laboratory Technician: Urd is your real name. If you want to find the true you, you need to accept it.

兀尔德？：我只是一名调查记者，偶尔给一些嬉皮士写一写传记。“兀尔德”只是我用来给特定杂志投稿的笔名。
Urd?: But I'm just a journalist, an occasional writer on hippies. Urd is simply a pseudonym for my submissions to a certain magazine.

兀尔德？：我不知道这些实验的意义，你们口中那些“为了世界和平”的话，倒很像我的一些在街头生活的客户……
Urd?: I still don't understand the purpose of this experiment. Your claims of "world peace" sound no different from many of my interviewees on the street.

实验人员：她已经准备好了。
Laboratory Technician: She's ready.

实验人员：那么，第13次灌体实验，开始——
Laboratory Technician: Vessel ensoulment test number 13, begin.

兀尔德：——维尔汀？
Urd: Vertin?

维尔汀：……妈妈？
Vertin: Mum?

兀尔德：真的是你，孩子……
Urd: It really is you, my child.

兀尔德：好久没有见面了，你的样子比我预想中的要瘦弱许多。但你长大了，这真的太好了。
Urd: It's been so, so very long. You're slighter than I'd imagined, but how wonderful it is to see how you've grown.

维尔汀：为什么你会在这里？这不是现实，我能感觉得到……你在哪里？我之后要去哪里才能找到你？
Vertin: Why are you here? This isn't reality. I can feel it. Where are you really? Where can I find you?

兀尔德：不要流泪，孩子……
Urd: Don't cry, my child.

兀尔德：此刻只是过往的一瞬，我只能告诉你一些有关过去的事——
Urd: This is but a moment from the past. I can only tell you what has already happened.

？？？：灌体实验成功了？
???: Was the ensoulment successful?

实验人员：接近成功。太令人惊叹了，之前所有的受试个体，全都无法承受实验的副作用，只有兀尔德——
Laboratory Technician: Not quite, but it's the closest we've ever gotten. Amazing, all previous subjects couldn't bear the side effects of the experiment, only Urd—

？？？：说结论。
???: State the conclusion.

实验人员：——是。在第13次实验时，兀尔德的人格也许曾在一瞬间回归。
Laboratory Technician: Yes, sir. Urd's true personality may have briefly returned during the 13th test.

实验人员：证据是琥珀屋突然消失了。换一个说法，琥珀屋突然变得无法观测，视觉和其他反馈信号全部中断。
Laboratory Technician: We know this because of the disappearance of the Amber Room. That is to say, for a few seconds, the Room became unobservable. All feedback signals were cut off.

实验人员：这种情况持续了数秒。我猜，是兀尔德借用这一瞬间的回归，让琥珀屋前往了未来。
Laboratory Technician: My assumption is that the Amber Room traveled into the future during that time.

？？？：未来？——她要去未来做什么？
???: The future? Why? For what?

……
...

？？？：那就只有在未来才知道了。
???: Only time will tell.

……
...

？？？：司辰……
???: Timekeeper.

？？？：司辰？
???: Timekeeper?

维尔汀：呃嗯……
Vertin: Er ...

？？？：——司辰！您醒了吗？
???: Timekeeper! Are you awake?

不知是自己，还是身下的土地都在摇晃。耳旁混乱的轰鸣让人感觉如同被抛向了一场飓风。
Whether it's the ground beneath her or herself that is shaking, she can't tell. With the clamor of noises around her, it's as though she's just been thrown into a hurricane.

玛尔纱：十四行诗，司辰还好吗？
Marsha: Sonetto, is the Timekeeper alright?

十四行诗：司辰……她醒过来了！
Sonetto: She's awake!

维尔汀：……十四行诗，玛尔纱？
Vertin: Sonetto, Marsha?

大脑还停留在另一个时空，眼睛已经开始确定身体的位置。
Her mind still lingers in another time while her eyes struggle to grasp where she truly is.

维尔汀：到底发生什么事了？别列格勒……
Vertin: What's happening? Is Bereggrad ...

十四行诗：别列格勒在一小时前遭到格鲁托夫军队的突然袭击，一些匪军的士兵在空中轰炸的掩护下进入了城市。
Sonetto: Krutov launched a surprise attack on Bereggrad an hour ago. Some bandits have broken into the city under the cover of their air force.

十四行诗：骑兵军和民兵正在防守城市，伊戈尔也去联络自己的军队增援了。我们需要尽快转移到安全地带。
Sonetto: The cavalry and the militia have formed a defense. Igor went to contact his people for reinforcements. We need to get you to safety as soon as possible.

维尔汀：我应该……只在下面待了十五分钟才对。
Vertin: How long was I down there? 15 minutes, right?

十四行诗：不，司辰，您已经……在下面消失了十二个小时了。我刚刚才把您从地下带出来。
Sonetto: 15 minutes? Timekeeper, you ... you've been gone for almost 12 hours. I just brought you back above ground.

维尔汀：……
Vertin: ...

玛尔纱：司辰，虽然现在这么问有些勉强，但是——你可以行动了吗？
Marsha: Timekeeper, sorry for asking so soon, but are you able to move?

维尔汀：我没问题，马上……就能站起来。
Vertin: Yes, I'm fine. Just give me one more minute.

玛尔纱：好的，眼下的情况是，格鲁托夫攻城的先锋部队占领了部分外围城区。
Marsha: Alright. Here's the situation: Krutov's vanguard has occupied part of the outskirts.

玛尔纱：这座小修道院还在友军控制区内，但是坚持不了多久了。我们需要撤退到下一个街区。
Marsha: Though this church is currently within the safe zone, it won't be for long. We need to retreat a few streets back.

玛尔纱：有一支小部队在十分钟前切断了我们的退路，稍后我会尝试突围，打开一条连接修道院和民兵据点的路线。
Marsha: Ten minutes ago, a small force cut off our retreat. I'll attempt to break through a route connecting us to the militia's stronghold.

玛尔纱：等待我的信号，司辰！
Marsha: Wait for my signal, Timekeeper.

玛尔纱：——！
Marsha: ...!!

堑壕棒不失为狭小空间中肉搏的利器，骑士很快在有敌军把守的巷道中打开了一条通路。
The knight's trench club proves an effective weapon in the cramped alleys of the city. It isn't long before Marsha has cleared a path.

玛尔纱：司辰，十四行诗，快到我这儿来！
Marsha: Timekeeper! Sonetto! This way, quick!

十四行诗：司辰，请抓紧我。
Sonetto: Timekeeper, please hold onto me.

维尔汀：嗯……
Vertin: Alright.

一半的重量压在第一助手身上，她仍然以惊人的速度穿越了开阔而危险的主要街道。
Even with half her weight on her, Sonetto manages to cross the open danger of the main street with astonishing speed.

玛尔纱：巷子的另一头就是骑兵军和别列格勒民兵占领的街区了，他们会带你们出城去安全的地方。
Marsha: At the other end of this alley is the area under our control. The Cavalry Corps will escort you out of the city to a safe place.

十四行诗：你不和我们一起离开吗，玛尔纱女士？
Sonetto: Aren't you leaving with us, Ms. Marsha?

玛尔纱：我会把你们带到军长身边，但是在敌军从城市里被赶出去之前，我会留在别列格勒，为这里的人出一份力。
Marsha: I'll take you to the commander. But after that, I'll stay in Bereggrad until the enemy is repelled.

轰炸机的残骸插在修道院的圆顶上，是刚刚被伊戈尔部队的防空高炮击落的。
The wreckage of a warplane shot down just moments ago by Igor's anti-aircraft guns lies lodged in the dome of a church.

在此之前，它和它的伙伴已经将数枚炮弹送到了民兵营地、医院、修道院和民居，声势浩大地打破了堪堪维持住的平静。
Before that, several shells had been launched into the militia camp, hospitals, churches, and residences, setting the hard-kept peace ablaze.

梅蕾尔：自己人，是自己人，她们回来了！
Merel: Friendlies! It's friendlies! They're back!

梅蕾尔放下望远镜，呼唤着让守卫街垒的民兵让出一条路，把一支刚从交火线下来的队伍放进防线后方。
Merel lowers her binoculars and calls for the militia guarding the street fortifications to clear a path, allowing the three young women to fall back into the rear formation.

留守城内的指挥官闻声而至。
The commander strides forward at the sound of her voice.

军长伊万：你受伤了吗，司辰，看起来你的状态很不好？
Commander Ivan: Are you alright, Timekeeper? You don't seem well.

维尔汀：没关系，我没有受伤，只是有点头晕。
Vertin: It's okay. I'm not hurt. Just a bit dizzy.

十四行诗：司辰在地下待了十二个小时，没有吃任何东西，她的血糖值可能会因此出问题。我先带她去吃点东西。
Sonetto: The Timekeeper hasn't eaten anything for over 12 hours. Her blood sugar might be the problem. I'll take her to have some food.

军长伊万：十四行诗小姐，司辰就交给你照顾了。我希望你能把她带到城外的骑兵军塞契。
Commander Ivan: I see. When you finish, take her to the sich outside of the city.

军长伊万：别列格勒的巷战还会持续很久，还有随时可能到来的空袭，这里并不安全。
Commander Ivan: This fight will not end soon. The city is no place to linger.

十四行诗：好的，我很快会带司辰离开。
Sonetto: Yes, Commander. I'll take her away as soon as possible.

军长伊万：那就这样办。
Commander Ivan: Make it so.

军长点了点头，转向等候在旁的骑士——不知什么时候，被骑兵军救下的落水少女已经站在她身旁。
The commander nods and turns to the knight waiting nearby. Merel is standing at her side, unnoticed until now.

军长伊万：你之前说会留在别列格勒。
Commander Ivan: And you. You swore to stay in Bereggrad.

玛尔纱：是，我可以加入民兵团的救援队，很多留在城市里的医生没有自保的能力。
Marsha: Yes, sir. I can join the militia rescue team. Many medical staff in the city cannot defend themselves.

军长伊万：很好，骑兵军与狮鹫军的部分军医也会留在城内，希望你们能互相帮助。
Commander Ivan: Good. Medics of the Cavalry Corps and Gryphon Legion will stay as well. You'll aid each other.

玛尔纱：没问题。
Marsha: Of course.

梅蕾尔：我、我也跟你一起，玛尔纱。
Merel: I-I'm coming with you, Marsha.

玛尔纱：那你就认真听我说的话。
Marsha: Fine, but do as I say.

梅蕾尔：好……
Merel: Okay.

此刻，军长已经回头去找同样留在城里的伊戈尔。
The commander looks around for Igor. The two leaders agreed to stay in the city.

后者依然举着望远镜，正看向城门口。
Igor is standing nearby, still holding a telescope, his gaze fixed on the city gate.

将军注视城门的时间很长。
He doesn't move for a long time.

军长伊万：你在看什么？
Commander Ivan: What do you see?

城门之外只有一大片一大片金色的原野。
Beyond the gate lies only the vast golden plain.

伊戈尔：我了解格鲁托夫，他要想宣战，不会只送我们几枚炮弹和一架轰炸机。
Igor: I know Krutov. If this is his declaration of war, he will not stop at bombs and bombers.

军长伊万：什么意思？你是说……
Commander Ivan: What? You mean ...

伊戈尔：来了。
Igor: It's coming.

金黄的茅草伏低了下去，被疾驰的马蹄踩出的路直直地向城门而来。
The grass bows low as black galloping hooves carve a path straight to the city.

黑马上的骑士蒙着白布，握着一把染血的镖枪，正如光临迦太基城下的罗马祭司。
A cloth-covered rider bounces limply on the horse's back. He carries a blood-smeared javelin, like a Roman priest riding toward Carthage.

伊戈尔：派来宣战的信使，真是古典的桥段。
Igor: A messenger bearing a declaration of war. Hm. A classic move.

军长伊万：可惜派来了一个不会骑马的骑兵。
Commander Ivan: A pity the man doesn't know how to ride.

信使没有抓住缰绳，在风中摇摇欲坠，如一面不祥的旗帜。黑马兀自向城门奔驰而来。
The messenger does not grip the reins. He jostles and sways, like an ominous banner battered too strongly by the wind. But the black horse only gallops faster, pummeling straight for the gate.

玛尔纱：这个人……
Marsha: That's ...

当信使与他的黑马来到城门口，骑兵们已经一字排开，用枪口迎接他。
By the time the messenger arrives, the cavalry have already formed ranks, guns trained on him.

但信使既没来得及朗读宣战书，也没有掷下染血的镖枪。
But the messenger reads no declaration of war, nor does he throw the bloodstained javelin.

不多时，信使坠向地面，黑马在一旁徒劳而哀苦地嘶吼着。
He only slides from the horse and crashes to the ground, his shattered form laid bare. The horse rears and lets out a mournful whinny.

梅蕾尔：……卡戎，安德烈森？！
Merel: Charon? Andreas?!

玛尔纱：真的是——
Marsha: I-Is that really—

红发骑士与她的同伴终于看清了来人的样子。她们一起冲向城门口，破开骑兵的包围。
They finally realize who it is. They rush to the gate, charging through the ring of cavalrymen.

梅蕾尔：——！
Merel: ...!

看见卡戎的第一眼，梅蕾尔陡然跌坐在地，双手紧紧抱住自己的脑袋。
The instant Merel lays eyes on Charon, she crumples to the ground, her arms wrapped tightly around her head.

梅蕾尔：不……不要——！
Merel: No. Don't—!

骑兵们勉强围成一圈，而战马惊恐地往后退。它们也嗅到了“死亡”的气息。
The cavalry barely manages to hold formation as the warhorses shy back, champing and stamping their feet. They, too, can smell the stench of "death."

玛尔纱：不对——不要靠近，快散开，不要去看他！梅蕾尔，到我这儿来！
Marsha: Something isn't right. Don't get close, understood? Don't look at him! Merel, come to me!

她扑向梅蕾尔，将她拖到一处掩体之后，隔绝她与卡戎之间的视线。
She lunges to Merel's side and drags her behind cover, blocking her view of Charon.

其他骑兵也在一阵阵令人作呕的哀嚎声中四散溃逃。
The cavalrymen scatter as wave after wave of nauseating howling washes over them.

此时此刻，城门边的守军不得不撤离，别列格勒门户洞开，唯有“死亡”的气息充实其间。
The guards at the city gate have no choice but to fall back. Entry to Bereggrad lies wide open, filled with nothing but the stench of "death."

玛尔纱：……必须要有人把卡戎带到封闭的场所。
Marsha: *deep breath* Someone needs to take Charon to an enclosed space.

玛尔纱：好吧，也许我可以试试。
Marsha: I suppose I'll have to give it a try.

骑士深吸一口气，像过去千百次那样将情绪冻结。她尽量不去想，今天积累的恐惧要在什么时候释放出来。
Just as she has done countless times before, Marsha draws a deep breath and stills her emotions, paying no heed to what may happen when she finally releases whatever fear she is soon to face.

她安抚地拍了拍身旁的梅蕾尔，随后走出掩体，一步步迈向“死亡”笼罩的深渊，直视着卡戎倒地不起的身躯。
She gives Merel a gentle pat on the shoulder and steps out from behind the shelter. She walks toward the abyss of "death," looking directly at Charon's fallen body.

杏仁核中的恐惧感被如期阻断。
The fear in her amygdala is severed, just as promised.

玛尔纱：奏效了。
Marsha: It's working.

玛尔纱：卡戎……天呐，他们对你做了什么？
Marsha: Charon, oh my, what have they done to you?

在她眼前的是一副无法描摹的碎裂躯壳，好像再也经不起任何更进一步的触碰。
What lies before her is barely recognizable. It isn't a body. It's a shattered, indescribable shell.

卡戎显然是被绑在马上送到别列格勒来的——感谢这些染血的绳索，他才堪堪维持住了类似于人的形状。
It is only by virtue of the blood-soaked ropes that he has managed to maintain any semblance of a human form.

失去了遮掩物，又脱离了完整躯体的压制，“死亡”正丝丝缕缕从收尸人的衣袍下溢出。
With his coverings gone, and freed from the constraints of a complete form, "death" seeps out from beneath Charon's clothes.

亡者身下的土地正肉眼可见地被浓雾浸染，黑色的军阀将“死亡”的宣告送至别列格勒。
The soil beneath him visibly darkens, the air around it swallowed in a heavy fog. Krutov has brought a declaration of death to Bereggrad.

卡戎：……
Charon: ...

玛尔纱：你刚刚是在说话吗，卡戎？
Marsha: Yes, Charon? What is it?

玛尔纱俯下身，离卡戎更近了一点，以便听到他朽坏的身躯尚且能发出的声音。
Marsha leans in close in an attempt to catch whatever sound his ruined body is still able to give voice to.

卡戎：……一个不幸的消息，我不得不……带给城里的人们……
Charon: A message from Krutov.

卡戎：格鲁托夫的军队马上就要攻破别列格勒，他……会将城市夷为平地……除非……
Charon: He swears to destroy Bereggrad, unless ...

卡戎：……交出伊戈尔。
Charon: You hand over Igor.

12TH-12 生活与命运 / Life and Fate

他不像生者那般会感受到痛苦，但痛苦很明显在他身上留下了烙印。他一定经历过难以想象的折磨。
He does not feel pain as the living do, but it has left its mark all the same. He must have endured unimaginable torment.

玛尔纱：整个身体的结构都被破坏了，神秘术能量严重外泄，这进一步导致了虚弱……
Marsha: His bodily structure is too fractured to store his arcane energy. The leakage is worsening his condition.

卡戎身躯的组合方式十分别扭，像一个人被粉碎了一千次，各个零件无法如常拼合到一起。
Charon's body is held together in an unnatural way. Like a man crushed a thousand times, his fragments no longer fit together as they should.

玛尔纱：重塑之手怎么能做出这种事。
Marsha: How could the Manus do such a thing?

梅蕾尔：为什么……他明明和这个地方毫无关系，为什么连卡戎也被……
Merel: Why? He's got nothing to do with any of this.

梅蕾尔背向着卡戎站立，她缩起的肩膀正微微发颤。
Merel stands with her back to Charon, her shoulders hunched and trembling.

梅蕾尔：我应该和你一起走的，卡戎。
Merel: I should've gone with you, Charon.

和此地毫无瓜葛的朋友正躺在担架上。他总是沉默、自持，像一堵墙，静静伫立在所有人身后。
Charon now lies on a stretcher. Silent and contained, like a black wall behind them.

经历漫长旅途之后，梅蕾尔今天第一次见到了卡戎的神秘术——庞大，空洞，如同死亡本身。
Merel finally saw Charon's arcane skill for the first time. Vast and hollow, like death itself.

梅蕾尔：不……
Merel: No ...

玛尔纱：梅蕾尔……梅蕾尔？
Marsha: Merel. Merel?

梅蕾尔：玛尔纱……我——
Merel: Marsha, *sniffle* I ...

她本能地想回头，红发骑士的双手立刻扣在她的肩上，把她拧了回去。
She instinctively turns to her, but Marsha grips her shoulders firmly, holding her back in place.

玛尔纱：别转身，我只是想提醒你打起精神，卡戎似乎想说些什么。
Marsha: Don't turn around. I think Charon wants to tell you something.

梅蕾尔：你……你想说什么，卡戎？
Merel: What? What is it, Charon?

卡戎：……梅蕾尔……
Charon: Merel ...

梅蕾尔：别、别说了，是我不好！
Merel: *sob* Charon, I'm sorry! It's all my fault!

仅仅一个词语，就让她的话如决堤河水，汹涌而出。
With a single word, Merel's words come rushing like a river breaking its banks.

梅蕾尔：我们一起走了这么久，这么远，我害你和我一起东躲西藏，最后……最后遇到危险我就丢下你不管了。
Merel: You protected me, walked with me all this way, hid me, kept me safe, and ... and after all that, after everything you've done for me, I left you there all alone!

梅蕾尔：我要是再厉害一点，就能把你一起带走，或者从别人手上把你救回来，可是……
Merel: If only I weren't such a weakling, if only I were brave like the others, I could've taken you with me, saved you for once.

梅蕾尔：可是……可是……
Merel: But ... but ...

梅蕾尔：是我太没有用了……对不起，是我害了你和安德烈森……对不起，我……你可能不会变成这样的——
Merel: It's all my fault. I'm useless. I should never have left you behind. If it weren't for me, you could've ... you could've ...

梅蕾尔：呜……
Merel: *whimper*

更多的话还没有说出口，它们全都一股脑地哽在她的喉咙里。
The words choke in her throat before they can be spoken.

卡戎：……不，梅蕾尔……
Charon: No, Merel ...

卡戎这才有机会重拾破碎的言语。
Charon finds a chance to piece together his broken speech.

卡戎：你答应过我，遇见危险就会逃走……
Charon: You promised to run away when danger came.

卡戎：为什么你现在还……留在这里？为什么不去更远的……更安全的地方……？
Charon: Why do you remain here? Go. Find a safe place.

梅蕾尔：但我……已经没办法逃跑了。不，我不应该逃走的。
Merel: No. I can't. I can't run away anymore. I shouldn't.

梅蕾尔：从、从最开始，我就不应该逃走的。
Merel: I should never have run in the first place.

梅蕾尔：如果我老老实实地归队，如果我没说要和你一起走……如果……
Merel: If I'd just gone back to the squad, if I hadn't asked to go with you, if ...

梅蕾尔：呜……呜……
Merel: *whimper*

梅蕾尔又伤心得说不出话了。
Merel is too overwhelmed to speak.

有一双手拭去了她满面的泪水。
A pair of hands gently wipes the tears from her face.

玛尔纱：你哭成这样，我还怎么指望你和我一起把卡戎治好？
Marsha: Hush now. How are you supposed to help me fix Charon up if you keep crying like this?

梅蕾尔：……
Merel: ...

玛尔纱：别忘了我们要做的事。
Marsha: Don't forget what we need to do.

玛尔纱：卡戎不会有事的，只要意识的载体能够复原，他应该就能慢慢恢复过来。
Marsha: Charon will be fine. As long as we can restore the vessel of his consciousness, he'll recover.

玛尔纱：现在只有我能面对卡戎，而我需要一个信得过的助手，也就是说，这里能帮他的只有我们两个了，明白了吗？
Marsha: I'm the only one who can look at him right now, and I need a reliable assistant. Only the two of us can help him. Do you understand?

梅蕾尔：对……没错，我明白。
Merel: Yes. *sniff* Right. I understand.

玛尔纱：那么，休息一下，擦擦眼泪。
Marsha: Then take a moment and wipe your tears.

玛尔纱：整个过程不会很轻松，但很快就会结束。
Marsha: It won't be an easy task, but it'll soon be over.

玛尔纱：听我的指令，我要什么东西就立刻递给我，能做到吗，梅蕾尔？
Marsha: Just follow my instructions and give me what I need when I ask for it. Can you do that, Merel?

少年踩在倒塌的石柱上，身后是插在修道院房顶的轰炸机。
A boy steps onto a fallen stone pillar, the wreckage of the warplane in the church behind him.

飞机被击落了，但它的身子依然耀武扬威，时刻提醒着这座城市有多么脆弱。
It's been shot down, yet it still seems to posture in defiance—a grim reminder of how fragile this city is.

市民代表：别列格勒不能成为牺牲品！
Citizen Representative: We will not be victims!

市民们：别列格勒不能成为牺牲品！
Citizens: We will not be victims!

许多人围着费奥多尔·彼得罗维奇，彼此紧挨着，成了一个紧密的圈。
One by one, people gather around Fyodor Petrovich, quickly forming a tight circle.

市民代表：保护别列格勒！交出伊戈尔！
Citizen Representative: Save Bereggrad! Hand over Igor!

市民们：交出伊戈尔！
Citizens: Hand over Igor!

不断有零星的人靠近他们，成为圈的一部分。
More and more voices join the chanting.

剩下的居民在不远的地方看着，没有加入示威的圆环。有人掩面私语，有人抬起头，忧心忡忡地看着即将落下炸弹的天空。
The rest of the residents linger at a distance. Some whisper behind covered mouths. Others lift anxious eyes to the sky, searching for bombs that may yet fall.

示威的市民翻越街巷上堆砌的障碍物，终于在城防指挥部前的街垒前被黑洞洞的枪口拦下。
The chanting crowd clambers over the street barricades, only to be halted by gun barrels before the fortifications of the city defense headquarters.

谢尔盖：别往前走！
Sergey: Stop! Don't go any further!

市民代表：滚开，你这胡子还没长齐的小毛孩。我要和你们的军长说话。
Citizen Representative: Stand aside, kid. I need to talk to your commander.

谢尔盖：你要说就在这儿说，我给你传话。
Sergey: You can tell me. I'll pass it on.

谢尔盖察觉到身侧有人推了他一把。
Sergey feels a shove from the side.

民兵：我认得这人，小子，我来和他说。
Militiaman: Hey, I know this man. Let me talk to him.

别列格勒民兵攀上街垒，好站得更高些。
The Bereggrad militiaman climbs onto the fortifications, standing taller.

民兵：费奥多尔，带着你的人滚回去吧！还是说，你就是要来给我们添乱的？
Militiaman: Fyodor, take your people and turn back! Or are you here just to cause trouble?

市民代表：迪马，你怎么还和骑兵军站在一起？我告诉你吧，民兵团有好多人都站在我们这边了。
Citizen Representative: Still standing strong with the cavalry, are we, Dima? Don't you know how many have sided with us?

民兵：他们就是一些没断奶的羊，被人一声吼就吓得四脚朝天了。
Militiaman: Them? Pah, just little sheep following any dog that barks at them!

市民代表：真是说不通道理——只要把那个叫伊戈尔的人交出去，格鲁托夫就不烧咱们的城。为什么不做这个买卖呢？
Citizen Representative: You idiots! All we have to do is hand over that Igor, and Krutov will leave us be! The choice is obvious!

谢尔盖：你这城里人，白痴，土匪的话也听！
Sergey: You're the idiot! They're bandits! You can't trust a word they say!

市民代表：那你又知道这伊戈尔是什么玩意？
Citizen Representative: And this Igor? Who is he?

市民代表：顿河上下有谁认识伊戈尔？把他送出去又有什么坏处？骑兵军说要守城，那把伊戈尔交出去，这事不就完了？
Citizen Representative: No one here has ever even heard of him. It's no skin off our back to hand him over. You cavalry said you wanted to protect the city. Now is your chance!

市民代表：伊戈尔和格鲁托夫有恩怨，就让他们自己到草原上解决。
Citizen Representative: If Krutov has some personal issue with Igor, then I say they solve it themselves on the steppe!

谢尔盖：你什么都搞不明白，大叔，我一看你这鼻子，就知道你早就把自己的脑子喝坏了。
Sergey: You don't know what you're talking about. The drink's pickled your brain. Just look at your nose.

谢尔盖：别在这里废话了，我听着都头疼。这事要怎么做，难道还是你说了算呀？
Sergey: You've got no say here anyway. So shut it and go home.

人群爆发出一阵嘈杂的、无法辨认内容的嘘声。
A cacophony of boos erupts from the crowd.

民兵：有这股热情劲儿，倒是带你们的人去把土匪占着的鱼市场夺回来啊！
Militiaman: Or you can use your enthusiasm to fight off the bandits and get our market back.

军长收回了投向窗外的目光。
The commander turns from the window.

军长伊万：告诉一营营长，让他带上几个机灵点儿的兵去疏散堵在外面的市民。
Commander Ivan: Tell the first battalion's commander to evacuate the citizens trapped outside. Just a few sharp soldiers. Don't worsen the situation.

军长伊万：记住，别擦枪走火了。费奥多尔不敢真的动手，他还要留着命享受家里数不完的钱。
Commander Ivan: Be careful. No misfires. Fyodor won't dare start a real fight. He'd sooner roll in his wealth than die.

斯捷尔诺娃：是。
Sternova: Yes, Commander.

斯捷尔诺娃带着命令离去。
Sternova leaves at the order.

军长伊万：格鲁托夫不愧是你的人，伊戈尔。
Commander Ivan: You taught Krutov well, Igor.

军长伊万：这离间的计策老套但有效，我们的士兵不擅长巷战，保卫别列格勒需要依靠民兵团和市民的配合。
Commander Ivan: He has driven a wedge between us. Old-fashioned, but effective. He knows we need both the militia and the citizens to hold Bereggrad.

军长伊万：格鲁托夫把你的名字抛出来后，至少有一半人失去了对我们的信任。
Commander Ivan: One whispered deal, and half turn against us.

伊戈尔：他会用一切方法让我死得更狼狈一点。
Igor: He will do anything to bring me a humiliating death.

军长伊万：为什么格鲁托夫这么执着地要你的命？我以前确实和他处不来，看不出他这么恨你。
Commander Ivan: Why? I never warmed to him, true, but I had no inkling his hatred ran so deep.

伊戈尔沉默半晌，像是要在一处黑暗的深潭中捞取思绪。
Igor falls silent, as if fishing his thoughts from the depths of a dark pond.

伊戈尔：他和我一样，在圣保罗之后都无法再回头，只能在认定的路上走下去。
Igor: Like me, there was no turning back for him after São Paulo. He can only continue down the path he has laid.

伊戈尔：与重塑之手达成一次性的交易之后，他怨恨我给的不够多，不值得他与我一同做出那些所谓“正确的牺牲”。
Igor: Since the deal with Manus Vindictae, he has resented me. He claims I shorted him for his sacrifice.

伊戈尔：格鲁托夫认为脱离重塑之手是一个巨大的错误，他希望从他们身上攫取更多力量。
Igor: He also believes our break from the Manus was a grave mistake. He wishes to wrest more power from them.

伊戈尔：不过，我承诺给他的从来都不是力量，而是生存。但他仍然不明白，以为“奇迹”是能让他接近神明的圣物。
Igor: But I never promised him power; I promised him a chance at survival. Still, he calls the "boon" a sacred thing that will grant him the power of a god.

伊戈尔：格鲁托夫把这种观念不合当成是我的软弱，执着于向我证明他的道路才称得上正确。
Igor: Krutov took my choice as weakness. Now, he is obsessed with proving that his path is the right one.

伊戈尔：……他一直都想杀死我，夺走我向重塑之手换来的“奇迹”，或者是向重塑之手证明自己的价值。
Igor: He wants to kill me, to take the "boon," to prove his worth to the Manus.

伊戈尔：所以，我们可以利用这种“执着”。
Igor: We can take advantage of this.

窗外的街道上，已经传来骑兵军与市民发生争执的声音。
Outside, arguments between the cavalrymen and citizens rise and fall along the street.

伊戈尔：有一点是没错的，决定性的战斗会在郊外发生。我们不能在城内久留。
Igor: One thing is certain: this decisive battle will not be inside the city. We cannot stay here long.

伊戈尔：一起出城吧，伊万。我们最好在回营地的路上就找到击败格鲁托夫的办法。
Igor: Let us leave together, Ivan. We will discuss our strategy on the way to camp.

12TH-13 诀别书 / Farewell Letter

斯捷尔诺娃：……那么，这就是你和伊戈尔商议的作战计划？
Sternova: So, you're saying you devised this plan with Igor?

斯捷尔诺娃与军长隔着地图桌相对而立，她焦躁地将用来代表军事力量的指示物挪来挪去。
Sternova stands opposite the commander, the map table between them. Agitated, she shifts the markers representing the military forces back and forth.

军长抬头看了她一眼，尽管后者并未言明，但她的态度不言而喻。
The commander glances up at her. Her words are minimal, but her stance is made clear.

军长伊万：把那个狮鹫放下吧，斯捷尔诺娃，现在我们和伊戈尔站在同一条船上。
Commander Ivan: Put the gryphon down, Sabina. We're all in the same boat now.

斯捷尔诺娃挥了挥手，把狮鹫木雕甩到了地图的边缘。
Sternova raises a hand and sweeps the wooden gryphon to the edge of the table.

斯捷尔诺娃：我非常认同你提出的作战计划，军长，但我仍然不认为可以放心地把后背交给伊戈尔。
Sternova: I'm not questioning your orders, but I will state for the record that leaving our back wide open to Igor is too risky.

斯捷尔诺娃：天黑后，让骑兵军放弃辎重，沿左岸向上游发动奇袭，清扫所有遭遇的敌方部队并切断格鲁托夫的补给路线。
Sternova: After dark, the cavalry will advance upstream with minimal gear to launch a surprise attack, cutting off Krutov's supply lines.

斯捷尔诺娃：——我不怀疑计划的可行性，骑兵们熟悉河岸的田地与山谷，我军的机动性能得到最大程度的发挥。
Sternova: It makes sense. Our riders know the terrain like the back of their hand; this will allow us to capitalize on our superior mobility.

斯捷尔诺娃：但把右岸林地、塞契与别列格勒的城防交给伊戈尔，让他来保护我们的后方——
Sternova: But we would be leaving the right bank, the forest, the sich, and even Bereggrad exposed.

斯捷尔诺娃：这和把羊肉送到狮子嘴里有什么区别？只要伊戈尔愿意，骑兵军随时会身处腹背受敌的境况。
Sternova: We're throwing ourselves into the old lion's mouth and praying he won't bite!

军长伊万：如果同盟的两军不能互相信任，那只会被逐一击破，任何作战计划都无从谈起。
Commander Ivan: You're right. We'd be exposed. But a coalition without trust wins nothing.

军长伊万：你已经见识过格鲁托夫的军队了，骑兵军和民兵团都没有能力应付敌人的空中力量和地面的重武器。
Commander Ivan: You've seen Krutov and his army. Neither the Cavalry Corps nor the militia can meet his air power or artillery.

军长伊万：如果没有伊戈尔带来的几台高射炮，别列格勒在第一轮空袭中就能被炸成废墟。
Commander Ivan: Bereggrad would be rubble if not for Igor's anti-air guns.

斯捷尔诺娃：……
Sternova: ...

她想起撤离别列格勒时，印在视野中的被航空炸弹削去半边拱顶的救济院。
Her thoughts drift to the poorhouse, its dome half-destroyed in a bomb dropped during their withdrawal from Bereggrad.

军长伊万：狮鹫军装备精良，但人数不多，而且没有建立完备的补给线。他们更适合依托城市和林地构筑防线。
Commander Ivan: The Gryphon Legion is well-equipped, but they're thin on numbers and supplies. They will hold cities and forests best.

军长伊万：所以，把城市和林地交给伊戈尔，骑兵军从侧翼找机会袭击敌军，我和伊戈尔都认为这是一个合理的选择。
Commander Ivan: Let them guard the city. Our riders will flank the enemy by night. Both Igor and I agree on this.

斯捷尔诺娃：但……
Sternova: But ...

她变得有些迟疑。她知道长官是对的，可南美洲的硝烟仍是笼罩在这场合作之上的阴霾。
She knows the commander has reasons, yet the smoke of South America still hangs heavy in her memory, casting an inescapable shadow over this coalition.

军长伊万：我理解你的疑虑。
Commander Ivan: I hear your concerns, Sabina.

军长拿起狮鹫木雕，让它降落在塞契。
He picks up the wooden gryphon and sets it down on the sich.

军长伊万：伊戈尔本人会留在骑兵军塞契，不会前往前线。而他与麾下部队的每一次通话都会处于我们的监控之下。
Commander Ivan: When the operation begins, Igor will come to our sich. All his communication will be monitored.

斯捷尔诺娃：我们的联络电台没有侵入伊戈尔方面线路的能力，要怎么窃听他？
Sternova: How? I doubt our operators can tap his lines so effectively.

军长伊万：不，我们不需要窃听他。在回营地的路上，我已经向伊戈尔提过公开通讯的要求。
Commander Ivan: There will be no such need. On our return from the city, I asked Igor to use only our lines for the operation.

军长伊万：他同意了。
Commander Ivan: He agreed.

斯捷尔诺娃：……
Sternova: ...

斯捷尔诺娃迟疑地点了点头。
Sternova nods hesitantly.

斯捷尔诺娃：我还是会盯着他的。
Sternova: I see. Still, I'll be keeping an eye on him.

伊戈尔：——我非常欢迎你的监督，上校。
Igor: Your scrutiny is welcome, Colonel Sternova.

不请自来的叛军将领走入营帐，踩在了参谋长本就紧绷的神经上。
The rebel leader enters the tent, his presence tightening the already frayed nerves of the chief of staff.

伊戈尔顶着斯捷尔诺娃审视的目光，将一份文件放在了沙盘上。
Under Sternova's piercing gaze, he places a document on the table.

斯捷尔诺娃：这是什么？
Sternova: What's this?

伊戈尔：我手上关于格鲁托夫本人的所有资料。履历、心理状态报告，以及他的神秘术登记表。
Igor: All the information I have on Krutov: his background, academic record, military experience, psychological profile, and a registered list of his arcane skills.

一份及时雨般的情报，同时也是一份绝佳的“诚意”。它成功让斯捷尔诺娃欲言又止，让合作得以延续。
The information comes like rain upon a desert. Such clear proof of good faith silences Sternova's worries. She silently agrees to allow the collaboration to continue.

军长伊万：好吧，过去我确实不太了解格鲁托夫。在开战之前，我会仔细看完你给我的资料。
Commander Ivan: Thank you. We know little of Krutov. I'll be sure to read this before we begin.

午前的烈日下，一些模糊的影子被投射在营帐的幕墙上。
Under the high noon sun, blurred shadows fall across the canvas wall of the tent.

斯捷尔诺娃：帐篷外有人？他们在做什么？
Sternova: Hm? Who's that gathering outside?

伊戈尔：我在进来之前，看见营地里有一些军官在商量什么事。也许聚在外面的就是他们。
Igor: I saw some officers discussing something in camp. It may be them.

军长伊万：莎宾娜，和我一起出去看看。
Commander Ivan: Let us hear what they have to say, Sabina.

斯捷尔诺娃：这是……
Sternova: This is ...

果然有不少人围在营帐之外——如伊戈尔所料，这些人大多都是军官。
Just as Igor predicted, there is a group of officers standing outside the tent.

他们手贴着裤缝，表情复杂，谨慎地站在距离帐门数米开外的地方。
Their hands rest along the seams of their trousers, their faces each wearing a complicated, cautious expression.

军长伊万：骑兵军马上就要出征了，你们像这样聚在一起，是想做什么呢？
Commander Ivan: Why are you out here jabbering when you should be making preparations?

第五团团长从队伍中向前一小步，行了一个标准的军礼。
The leader of the 5th Regiment takes a small step forward and delivers a textbook salute.

山羊胡骑兵：军长，我将代表军官和士兵们向您提出请求，希望得到您的首肯。
"Goat": Commander, I am here to make a request of you. On behalf of the men, sir.

军长伊万：说。
Commander Ivan: I'm listening.

军官代表深吸一口气。下巴上的山羊胡微微颤抖着。
He draws a deep breath. The goatee upon his chin trembles slightly.

山羊胡骑兵：军里有不少人的家就在附近，往返营地不过半天。他们希望能赶在动身之前，回家看一看亲人。
"Goat": As you know, many of our comrades have homes nearby—families. We formally request a half-day's leave to visit them.

山羊胡骑兵：我们不是害怕即将到来的战斗，哥萨克们都愿意为了顿河流干最后一滴血。
"Goat": I swear to you, sir. Not a single rider will shirk their duties. We are Cossacks, true, ready to shed blood on the battlefield.

山羊胡骑兵：因为我们的父母、祖父母，还有他们的父母与祖父母，都生活在草原上，都是骁勇的战士。
"Goat": We were born soldiers of the steppe, just as our fathers were, and theirs before them.

山羊胡骑兵：但我们也知道，明日的太阳升起后，很多人会死在战场上，这也许是他们最后一次与亲人见面的机会，所以……
"Goat": We know that not all of us will live to see the rising of the sun tomorrow. So, if we have a chance to see our loved ones ...

骑兵团长咬着牙，似乎忘记了准备好的、将要在军长面前说的话。
He clenches his teeth. Facing the commander, the speech he prepared seems to have slipped from his mind.

他干脆就此闭上嘴。毕竟最重要的请求已经给出。
So he simply remains silent. After all, the most important request has already been made.

军长伊万：……
Commander Ivan: ...

军长背过手，仿佛并未听见团长的请求。他的视线在一顶顶哥萨克军帽上掠过。
The commander clasps his hands behind his back, his gaze sweeping over the rows of Cossack military caps.

军官们追随着军长的视线，没有任何人敢打破这份寂静。
The soldiers follow his eyes. No one dares break the silence.

随后，他举起左手，置于耳旁，向后摆了摆手。
Then, he waves a hand.

军长伊万：半天能回营地的，允许回家探亲。快去快回。
Commander Ivan: A half-day. No more. Go see your families.

骑兵军官中爆发出一阵苦涩的欢呼。
A bittersweet cheer erupts from the soldiers.

营帐边的情绪很快向四周传递，营地内的其他士兵旋即从这股热烈的氛围中得知了军长的答复。
The feeling spreads quickly throughout the camp, the other soldiers soon learning of the commander's answer from the rising fervor.

斯捷尔诺娃：今晚出发前，我要看到全员在草原塞契归队，违者以逃兵论处！
Sternova: Anyone who fails to return to the sich before nightfall will be branded as a deserter. Do I make myself clear?

骑兵们在此起彼伏的“遵命”“谢谢”中离开了。军长长叹一口气，与斯捷尔诺娃对视了一眼。
The cavalrymen disperse to the tune of "Yes, sir" and "Thank you, sir." The commander lets out a long sigh and meets Sternova's eyes.

斯捷尔诺娃：你打算回红柳树村吗？
Sternova: Will you be paying a visit to Tamarovka?

军长伊万：不了。
Commander Ivan: No.

他摇了摇头。
He shakes his head.

军长伊万：进来吧，出发之前，我们还有不少事要处理。
Commander Ivan: There is much to prepare. Come. Let us return to it.

军长将一沓空白的信纸放在桌上，推向斯捷尔诺娃。
The commander sets a pile of blank letter paper on the table and pushes it toward Sternova.

军长伊万：传令给所有没有回家的人，留封信吧。
Commander Ivan: Pass these papers to any soldier not going home. Tell them to write a letter if they wish.

斯捷尔诺娃神色晦暗地看着信纸，又看了看桌后的军长与伊戈尔。
Sternova's gaze darkens. She glances at the commander, to Igor, and back again.

最后，她点了点头，抱着大半信纸退出了临时会议室。
Then, at last, she nods. She gathers the paper, turns, and leaves the makeshift meeting room.

伊戈尔：大战前允许士兵返乡，不是一位英明指挥官的举措。仁慈会挫伤士气，家人的关怀容易使士兵丧失斗志。
Igor: Not the wisest choice—sending them home just before a major operation. Their families will plead for them to stay.

军长伊万：他们会回来的，一个不落。你应该和我一样了解这群哥萨克。
Commander Ivan: But they will return. All of them. You share their blood, Igor, you should know this.

军长伊万：他们决不允许顿河变成流淌亲人鲜血的红河，这时候放他们回家，只会让士气烧得更猛烈。
Commander Ivan: And a Cossack will do anything to protect their home and family. The embrace of those they fight to protect will only sharpen their resolve.

军长淡然地为自己和临时盟友斟了杯添加了胡椒的黑茶。
The commander pours himself and his temporary ally a cup of dark tea spiced with pepper.

伊戈尔：你很信任他们，但他们甚至都不知道你真正的来历，也不明白芝诺想要他们做什么。
Igor: Maybe you think you know them, but they know little of you and even less about what Zeno expects of them.

伊戈尔：对家乡的眷恋会妨碍骑兵军真正的任务，总有一天他们会离开顿河，前往其他战场。
Igor: They will be sent to other battlefields, away from their homes. Their homesickness will be a liability.

军长伊万：这些话我在他们入伍的时候都已经说过了。新兵嘴上说明白，可心里始终不相信真有离开家乡的那一天。
Commander Ivan: They knew what service meant when they enlisted. Though, I cannot say if they are truly ready to leave their homeland behind.

伊戈尔：战火会平等地焚烧每一寸土地，但也会把军队中的纽带炼成牢不可破的锁链。看来你仍然相信这一点。
Igor: Homeland ... Every war is fought on someone's home, yet its name is used to forge the young into unbreakable soldiers. It seems you still understand this.

伊戈尔：那你呢，伊万？你为什么不回去一趟？往返红柳树村的路，在别列格勒城陷落前还算安全。
Igor: But tell me, Ivan, why don't you go to Tamarovka? The roads should still be safe.

军长伊万：……
Commander Ivan: ...

伊万拿起茶杯，啜饮一口。
Ivan lifts his cup and takes a sip.

伊戈尔：还是说，你终究认为1920年的顿河并不真正属于你，你也没有做好准备，告知你的士兵们关于时代的真相。
Igor: Or is it that the Don of this era is no home to you? Are you afraid to tell your soldiers the truth?

军长正了正制服领口，他在寻找一个可以岔开话题的方式。
The commander adjusts the collar of his uniform, searching for a way to change the subject.

军长伊万：我没必要向你解释什么。还有，在我这儿，你也享有和其他人相同的待遇。
Commander Ivan: Ha. I don't answer to you anymore, Igor. In fact, you're one of mine now. You should join them.

伊戈尔：什么意思？
Igor: Join them? What do you mean?

军长伊万：我是说，你也可以给自己的亲人写封信。
Commander Ivan: Write a letter to your loved ones.

意料之外的提议让伊戈尔陷入了沉默。
The unexpected proposal renders Igor silent.

军长伊万：格鲁托夫是冲着你本人来的，如果前线失利，你多半无法从战场脱身。
Commander Ivan: Krutov bears a grudge against you. It is clear. If we fail, he will show you no mercy.

军长伊万：那么，你没有需要道别的亲人吗？还是说，这个时代的一切，对你而言都是过眼烟云？
Commander Ivan: So, anyone to bid farewell to? Or is this era truly just a fleeting wind to you?

伊戈尔将热茶一口饮尽，起身，重新披上大衣。
Igor drinks the hot tea in one gulp. He rises and pulls on his coat.

伊戈尔：再见。
Igor: I'll leave you to your work.

军长伊万：希望战争结束后，我们不会再见面。
Commander Ivan: After this battle, Igor, I hope never to see you again.

伊戈尔从军长桌上取走了几张信纸，离开了营帐。
Taking a few sheets of letter paper from the commander's desk, Igor steps out of the tent.

军长独自站立着，仿佛在等待什么事情到来。不多时，接通指挥部的电台如预料般发出了警报般的提示音。
The commander remains standing, as if waiting for something to arrive. Soon, the radio linked to headquarters chirps its alarming tone as expected.

芝诺指挥部：布列科夫少将，司辰已经安全了吗？
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: Vice Admiral Burakov, is the Timekeeper safe?

军长伊万：司辰处在安全地点，她说已经初步完成了在别列格勒的任务。
Commander Ivan: Yes. She says her mission in Bereggrad is mostly complete.

芝诺指挥部：初步完成？那就够了，这足够我们向基金会的委员交差。
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: Good. We'll relay this to the Foundation Committee.

芝诺指挥部：你在顿河的任务结束了，立刻撤出该区域。
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: With that settled, your orders are to pull the Cavalry Corps from the region, effective immediately.

军长伊万：立刻？——原本的命令是在两周的时间内确保别列格勒的安全。骑兵军正在执行领受的任务。
Commander Ivan: Immediately? We were given two weeks to secure Bereggrad.

军长伊万：有一支受重塑之手援助的匪军正在威胁顿河地区，骑兵军会留下来解决他们之后再离开。
Commander Ivan: A warlord and his bandits, aided by Manus Vindictae, have been running rampant on the Don. We are working to neutralize this threat before redeployment.

芝诺指挥部：别列格勒和顿河在全局战略中并不重要。重塑之手的主力全在西线，在兵力有限的情况下，我们只能放弃。
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: Manus Vindictae's forces are concentrated on the Western Front. Our manpower is already stretched too thin. We can't afford to hold the Don River, not while there are more important strategic goals.

芝诺指挥部：我们没法给你两周时间了。
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: The decision is set. No two weeks.

军长伊万：那我只需要五天。五天之内，我就能解决顿河的问题，之后骑兵军会立即前往匈牙利。
Commander Ivan: Five days, that's all I ask. We will resolve the threat here and ride to Hungary without delay.

芝诺指挥部：解决？和伊戈尔的叛军一起解决？
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: And how do you plan to "resolve the threat"? With Igor's rebels?

军长伊万：……
Commander Ivan: ...

芝诺指挥部：不要以为指挥部不知道你和伊戈尔叛军的交往，为了司辰，伊里内伊的人可以睁一只眼闭一只眼。
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: Did you really think you could hide your coalition with Igor and his traitors? Irinei only turned a blind eye for the Timekeeper's sake.

芝诺指挥部：但既然司辰已经离开了，你继续和伊戈尔合作的理由是什么？
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: But the Timekeeper has finished her work, and you are still collaborating with them.

芝诺指挥部：如果委员会发起质询，你想好了要怎么回答吗？
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: Are you prepared to face the Committee if they demand an explanation?

军长伊万：…………
Commander Ivan: ...

芝诺指挥部：布列科夫少将？
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: Vice Admiral Burakov, do you read me?

芝诺指挥部：伊万·伊万诺维奇，你听见我说的话了吗？
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: Ivan Ivanovich, you understand what I'm saying, don't you?

芝诺指挥部：伊万，你会酿成大祸的！
Zeno Command Liaison Officer: You'll obey orders, or you'll face the consequences, Ivan!

军长伊万：……我和我的骑兵军会保卫我们的家乡，我们的家人，所以我选择与伊戈尔的叛军合作。
Commander Ivan: To protect our home and kin. That is why I stand with Igor's rebels.

军长伊万：这是我在军事法庭上会给出的答复。
Commander Ivan: That will be my only answer to the tribunal.

12TH-14 远征前夜 / The Night Before War

十四行诗推门而出。午后的风从草原深处吹来，带着不合时宜的干热。她站住脚，望着那片广袤无垠的草原与天交际处的地平线。
Sonetto steps outside, looking out over the endless grassland and to the sky beyond. The afternoon wind rushes from across the steppe, carrying an unseasonable dryness.

风拂过橘色的长发。行程紧迫的疲惫、大战在即的肃穆与因责任感而紧绷的神经，难得地得到了舒缓。
It gently rustles through her hair. The weariness from her relentless schedule, the weight of the coming war, and the tension she bears from her responsibilities are, for a brief moment, faintly eased.

伊戈尔：十四行诗小姐。
Igor: Greetings, Ms. Sonetto.

十四行诗：……伊戈尔先生。
Sonetto: Mr. Igor.

见面的礼节十分生硬。这不妨碍硬朗的老将军背靠在不远处的树下，闭着眼睛聆听着什么。
Their greeting is awkward, yet it doesn't stop the tough old admiral from leaning against a tree not far away. He gently closes his eyes, as if listening for something.

他从什么时候开始站在那儿的？十四行诗将这个疑问吞入腹中。
How long has he been standing there? Sonetto swallows the question before it reaches her lips.

十四行诗：你在做什么？
Sonetto: What are you doing out here?

伊戈尔：我在听风拂过草地的声音，它像一种启示，能够在战争开始前平复我的心情。
Igor: There's a sound as the wind brushes over the grasslands. I find it eases my mind.

第一助手凝神感受着风经过的声音。半晌后，她才继续提问。
Sonetto focuses in on the same sound. After a moment, she resumes her questions.

十四行诗：你是来找司辰的，对吗？
Sonetto: You're here for the Timekeeper, is that right?

伊戈尔：她还在休息？看来那里面的东西给她带来了不小的冲击。
Igor: Is she still resting? What she saw in the Amber Room must have impacted her greatly.

考虑到眼前这位老人的特殊身份，十四行诗藏在身后的手握紧了术杖。
Aware of the old man's special status, Sonetto tightens her grip on the wand hidden behind her back.

伊戈尔：别太紧绷着神经，年轻人。我没有别的意思，只是希望和司辰谈一谈。
Igor: I only want to have a word with her. Nothing more.

伊戈尔：现在，我们是同一个阵营的盟友。
Igor: We're on the same side.

马靴踩过草地的声音从身后传来。
Footsteps crunch through the dirt behind them.

维尔汀：……在击败格鲁托夫前，我们暂时是盟友。
Vertin: For the time being, yes, until Krutov is defeated.

伊戈尔：是我有失考量，我没想到你留在琥珀屋里的时间会这么长。格鲁托夫的军队进攻时，我不得不去指挥军队。
Igor: I owe you an apology, leaving you in the Amber Room for so long. My troops needed their leader when Krutov attacked.

维尔汀：这没什么，你有你的责任，我也有面对风险的准备。十四行诗和玛尔纱留下来帮助了我。
Vertin: Think nothing of it. I was prepared for the risks. Besides, Sonetto and Marsha were there to help me.

伊戈尔：我想知道，你在琥珀屋中看到了什么？
Igor: What did you see there, in the Room?

开门见山的提问。
An overt question.

自亘古而来的恐惧没由来地侵袭了视野，几次深呼吸后，理智才稍稍从角落挤了回来。
A fear older than memory floods her vision. After a few deep breaths, reason slowly returns.

维尔汀：我见到了兀尔德，可她对自己的身份存有疑虑，而有一些声音坚持让她相信自己就是兀尔德。
Vertin: I believe it was Urd. She seemed unsure of that herself. There were others there trying to convince her of her own identity.

维尔汀：她经历了一场残酷的实验。在一个瞬间，她看到了我、认出了我，来到了我面前，之后又消失不见。
Vertin: She was being put through some kind of disturbing experiment, and for a brief moment, she caught sight of me. She walked towards me, then vanished.

维尔汀：我似乎经历了一场实验。不过，真正经历它的不是我，而是……兀尔德。
Vertin: I felt like I'd been put into some kind of experiment. But it wasn't me. It was Urd.

维尔汀：这场实验重复了很多次，每一次都会给她带去巨大的痛苦。这一切似乎都是为了把她转变为另外一个人。
Vertin: They ran the experiment over and over, each time Urd suffering immense pain. It all seemed designed to transform her into someone else.

维尔汀：我看见了一间纯白的房间，我从没见过那样的白色。兀尔德……她就坐在白色房间中的一把椅子上。
Vertin: I saw a pure white room, a kind of white I've never seen before. And Urd ... She was sat in a chair at the center of it.

维尔汀：之后，她在椅子上痛苦地挣扎。我想要帮助她，但什么也做不到。我们之间隔着一层打不破的东西。
Vertin: She was struggling, as if she were in pain. I wanted to help, but I couldn't reach her.

维尔汀：我还看见了很多……但都是一些我不能完全理解的画面。
Vertin: I saw other things, too, but they were blurry and fragmented.

伊戈尔：画面？我还以为他们撤离时把屏幕设备都搬走了。
Igor: The video clips? Then they didn't take their devices with them when they evacuated after all.

维尔汀：不，不是影像资料。
Vertin: No, whatever I saw wasn't footage.

维尔汀：有些事还没弄明白，我想要再回一次琥珀屋。
Vertin: I have to enter the Amber Room once more to make sense of what I saw.

伊戈尔沉吟片刻，摇了摇头。
Igor falls silent for a moment, then shakes his head.

伊戈尔：我不建议你这么做，别列格勒城内的巷战还在继续，哪一方都无法保证能长时间控制那座修道院。
Igor: I advise against it. There are still skirmishes being fought in the city. No one can guarantee the church will stay safe for long.

伊戈尔：骑兵军准备发动野战，红弩箭中尉还在外执行拔除术阵节点的任务，除了你的助手外，分不出任何人手保护你。
Igor: The Cavalry Corps is preparing for a surprise assault tonight. Lieutenant Lilya is in the field trying to locate and destroy the Manus's rites. Your assistant will be your only protection.

伊戈尔：司辰对重塑之手有特殊的意义——如果被他们发现你出现在别列格勒，他们一定会想尽办法劫持你。
Igor: You're too important, Timekeeper. If your presence in Bereggrad were exposed, the Manus will throw everything they have into capturing you.

伊戈尔：我不希望我和伊万的作战计划节外生枝。所以你必须待在安全的后方。
Igor: I cannot afford to let anything jeopardize our battle plan. You must stay hidden from the enemy until it is safe.

十四行诗：……
Sonetto: ...

伊戈尔：我不否认你的能力与忠诚，十四行诗小姐。但昨天的空袭宣告着别列格勒已经成了真正的战场。
Igor: Ms. Sonetto, I don't question your capability and devotion, but Bereggrad is a potential battlefield. It's too dangerous.

维尔汀：我明白了，在格鲁托夫被击败后，我会在琥珀屋等你。
Vertin: Good point. I'll be sure to return to the Amber Room only after you've defeated Krutov.

伊戈尔：战事很快就会结束。
Igor: It will be done soon.

维尔汀：不久前有士兵找到了我，拜托我送信给他仍在西线的兄弟，他觉得基金会成员的生还概率更高。
Vertin: A soldier came to me earlier today. He seemed to think a Foundation member would have a higher chance of surviving the battle and asked me to deliver a letter to his brother on the Western Front.

维尔汀：你写信了吗，伊戈尔先生？
Vertin: What about you, Mr. Igor? Did you write anything?

对方难以察觉地叹了口气，似乎有些难言之隐。
Igor lets out a sigh so faint it almost goes unnoticed. Clearly he is trying to conceal something.

维尔汀：如果你死在别列格勒，会有人很遗憾的——她原本打算亲手杀死你。
Vertin: I know someone who would be deeply upset were you to die here. She intends to end your life with her own hands.

伊戈尔揉了揉太阳穴，露出一个无可奈何的苦笑。
Igor rubs his temples and gives a helpless smile.

伊戈尔：洛佩拉？她还在基金会？
Igor: Lopera. Does the Foundation still keep her?

维尔汀：当然。芝诺对她的审查还没有结束，她暂时没法作为士兵参加任务。
Vertin: You could say that. She isn't allowed to return to her position as a soldier yet, not until Zeno's review is finished.

伊戈尔点了点头，以示意自己希望听到更多。
Igor nods, signaling he wants to hear more.

维尔汀：她在基金会过得还不错，交到了一些新朋友，也因为出老千为自己惹出了一些麻烦。
Vertin: She's made somewhat of a life for herself at the Foundation. Made friends and got into some trouble.

维尔汀：基金会为她指派了一位“指导员”，以约束她对骰子游戏的沉迷。
Vertin: They've assigned her an instructor to work on her dice game obsession.

伊戈尔：……很有洛佩拉的风格。
Igor: Pera, so typical of her.

维尔汀：作为信息交换，我也希望你解答我的一个疑问。
Vertin: There's something I'd like to know, too.

伊戈尔：请问。
Igor: Ask away.

维尔汀：军长曾邀请我去他家做客，红柳树村的一位夫人招待了我们。
Vertin: Commander Ivan invited me to his home in Tamarovka for a lunch. A lady hosted us.

维尔汀：他说那是他的“母亲”，但……
Vertin: He introduced her as his "mother," but something seemed off.

伊戈尔：她确实是伊万的母亲。
Igor: She is indeed Ivan's mother.

维尔汀：军长替她申请了“暴雨”庇护？
Vertin: Then, did Commander Ivan request shelter for her from the "Storm"?

伊戈尔：在找到这位夫人后，没错。
Igor: Yes, a request made not long after their reunion.

伊戈尔双手环胸，皱起了眉头。
Igor folds his arms across his chest, frowning.

伊戈尔：谁都没有预料到第一场“暴雨”的到来，哪怕是最有经验的占卜师。伊万的母亲和世界上绝大多数人一样，被第一场“暴雨”回溯了。
Igor: Not even the most capable diviners could have predicted the advent of the "Storm." As you suspected, Ivan's mother, like most at that time, was reversed during the first "Storm."

伊戈尔：但伊万找到这位夫人的时候，他和我说，他的“母亲”幸存了下来。他绝不会认错那些深壑般的皱纹，那张慈祥的脸。
Igor: Some time after that, Ivan rediscovered her. He told me that he knew it was her from the wrinkles on her face and her tender smile.

伊戈尔：伊万笃定这就是他的母亲。无论“暴雨”是什么，它都奇迹般地没有夺走他们的家。
Igor: He was certain that, by some miracle, his mother had survived the "Storm" and returned to him.

伊戈尔：身为司辰的你，应该知道这件事有多荒谬。
Igor: An improbable scenario, don't you think, Timekeeper?

维尔汀：……
Vertin: ...

一个似曾相识的巧合。
A familiar coincidence.

维尔汀：终有一天我会弄清楚“真相”，为了所有人，还有……我的母亲。
Vertin: One day, I'll uncover the truth about the "Storm," for everyone's sake, for my mother.

伊戈尔并未回应，而是以深邃的目光注视着草原上的波浪。
Igor doesn't answer. Instead, he fixes his gaze on the rolling waves of grass.

夜幕降临于草原。
Night falls over the steppe.

在嘈杂的马蹄声与呼喊声中，斯捷尔诺娃掀开了行营的门帘。
Amid the chaos of pounding hooves and shouting voices, Sternova lifts the tent flap.

十四行诗：上校，行军要开始了吗？
Sonetto: Colonel Sternova, is the Corps prepared to ride out soon?

斯捷尔诺娃：是的，骑兵军集结完毕，即将开始夜行。
Sternova: Yes. Our forces are assembled. We're ready to go.

斯捷尔诺娃：狮鹫军已经提前启程。三支防空小队已经驻扎在别列格勒，剩下的人正在前往城市北翼的维尔霍罗德岭一带。
Sternova: As for the Gryphons, three of their air defense squads have been stationed in Bereggrad, while the rest are heading to Vysokogorye, the mountain north of the city.

维尔汀：伊戈尔也和自己的军队一起去了？
Vertin: Is Igor marching with his army?

斯捷尔诺娃：这倒没有，行动的总指挥部还设在塞契，他和军长都在营帐里。
Sternova: No, both Igor and Commander Ivan will stay at the command post in the sich.

斯捷尔诺娃：红弩箭中尉提醒我回来检查你是不是还在——听说你很擅长偷偷溜走。
Sternova: I'm here to check on you at Lieutenant Lilya's request. She said you're good at slipping away and making people worry.

身后传来十四行诗的一声憋笑，然后她贴心地帮忙转移了话题。
Sonetto suppresses a laugh before deftly steering the conversation elsewhere.

十四行诗：守护城市的只有三支防空小队吗？
Sonetto: Three squads. That's all the city has for air defense?

斯捷尔诺娃：还有民兵。伊戈尔的人手不够多，骑兵军也不擅长争夺街道，城内的巷战只能依靠民兵了。
Sternova: That and the militia. With our reduced numbers and the danger of street battles, we have to rely on the support of armed citizens.

帐外的躁动愈演愈烈，已经可以从骑兵军的喧哗声中隐约听见军长吼出的号令。
Outside the tent, the agitation has only continued to build. The commander's orders ring out, half-lost in the swelling noise.

斯捷尔诺娃：司辰，如果你现在不离开顿河，那就请一定留在安全的地方。
Sternova: Timekeeper, for your own sake, I suggest you leave the Don. Or at least make sure you bunker down someplace safe.

斯捷尔诺娃：我得走了，战前动员马上开始。
Sternova: I'll take my leave of you now. Commander Ivan is about to rally the troops.

隐秘而热烈的氛围笼罩在夜空之下，血液中崇武的基因正不安地躁动着。
Beneath the night's sky, a hushed yet fervent atmosphere settles in. The soldiers' fighting spirits render them restless.

芝诺骑兵Ⅰ：没想到我竟然能有幸参与一场真正的战争……该死，我的手竟然在发抖！！
Zeno Cavalryman I: To think I get to fight a real war! God! My hands won't stop shaking!

芝诺骑兵Ⅱ：傻子！我警告你，不要对战争抱有浪漫的幻想，它会害死你的！
Zeno Cavalryman II: Keep your head on straight, you idiot, or you'll get yourself killed. There's nothing romantic about war!

芝诺骑兵Ⅱ：年轻的时候，我们连的那几个同乡的战友，老是幻想着打完胜仗后回到顿河，享受同乡的赞美，与家人团聚。
Zeno Cavalryman II: I've fought alongside many soldiers like you. Dreaming of glory, victory, and the praise of our people when we returned home.

芝诺骑兵Ⅱ：他们全死了，只有我活到了今天。我回村里给他们上了坟，祈祷他们在战场上庇佑我。
Zeno Cavalryman II: But I returned alone. The rest died on some godforsaken battlefield, along with their dreams of glory. I visited their graves before I left. Hope their spirits are with me.

芝诺骑兵Ⅰ：……我也回去了。我去见了我喜欢的姑娘。
Zeno Cavalryman I: I-I went home too, to see my girl.

芝诺骑兵Ⅱ：你小子不会是说了什么打赢就回家结婚的鬼话吧？
Zeno Cavalryman II: You didn't promise you were going to marry her after we win the war, did you?

芝诺骑兵Ⅰ：不，我什么也没说……我只是看着她的眼睛，她就明白了我的意思。
Zeno Cavalryman I: No, I ... I didn't say anything at all. I just looked into those beautiful eyes of hers. She understood the rest.

芝诺骑兵Ⅰ：我们都知道，这可能就是最后一面了。
Zeno Cavalryman I: We knew it could be the last time we'd see each other.

芝诺骑兵Ⅱ：……得了，闭嘴吧，军长要说话了！
Zeno Cavalryman II: Alright, that's enough, lover boy. Commander Ivan's about to give his speech.

军长伊万：全军听令，清点人马！
Commander Ivan: Attention all troops! Call the roll!

雄浑而整齐的列阵声震耳欲聋，马儿们迎合着巨响，用蹄子敲响大地。
Strong, unified voices rise from the formations, joined by the thunder of horses stamping the ground.

斯捷尔诺娃：申请返乡的士兵们全员归队，军长。我就知道，骑兵军没有一个懦夫。
Sternova: All soldiers have returned to their posts, sir. I knew there were no cowards in the Corps.

军长伊万：我从没有为这件事担心过。
Commander Ivan: I expected nothing less.

军长伊万：——士兵们，想必你们都已经见识过格鲁托夫和他手下匪军的所作所为。
Commander Ivan: Listen, riders! You've seen the ruin Krutov and his bandits have wrought.

军长伊万：这些黑心肠的懦夫，以为有了偷来的武器，就能肆意践踏哥萨克的家园，杀害哥萨克的亲人。
Commander Ivan: You've seen those black-hearted cowards burn Cossack homes and kill our kin.

芝诺骑兵Ⅰ：那是个大言不惭的小丑！我要把他的脑袋挂在后院的树上！
Zeno Cavalryman I: I'm going to cut off that clown's head and hang it in my backyard!

年轻气盛的声音引来了一阵哄笑，随之而来的是无数扬起的拳头，以及无数赞同的呵声。
The young voice sparks a burst of laughter. Then fists and shouts of approval are thrown into the air.

军长伊万：你们看见了——黑色的军队掠夺了我们的亲人、同胞、粮食、土地，乃至尊严。尸体在河畔堆积成山。
Commander Ivan: You've seen them rob and trample our land, our people, and our dignity!

军长伊万：你们听见了——他们像豺狼一样等待夜色，把孩子们的哭声当成酒后的欢歌。
Commander Ivan: You've heard them laugh as they slaughtered our people and our children wept!

军长伊万：可是，同胞们，他们遇上的是谁？
Commander Ivan: But today their villainy ends. Why, my brothers and sisters?

军长伊万：是我们，是骑兵军，是草原的战马，是喝着顿河的水长大的儿女，是人民最后的仰仗！
Commander Ivan: Because we—the Cavalry Corps, riders of the steppe, children of the Don—will stop them in their tracks!

军长伊万：我们要用一场胜利彻底把他们打垮。为了草原，为了顿河，为了还未出世的孩子们——
Commander Ivan: We will grind them to dust and ride home victorious! For the steppe! For the Don! For Cossack children yet unborn!

军长伊万：扬起马蹄，冲吧！冲垮敌人的阵线，把他们赶出我们的草原！
Commander Ivan: Today, we destroy the enemy and reclaim our home! Forward!

众士兵：冲啊！
Soldiers: Ura!

随着军长的号令，骑兵的阵列开始移动。排头的侦察兵们高高地举起了火把。

这片属于哥萨克人的大地正为它儿女们的士气所颤抖。
This land, the great mother of the Cossacks, trembles beneath the vigor of her sons and daughters.

随着军长的号令，骑兵的阵列开始移动。排头的侦察兵们高高地举起了火把。
At the commander's order, the cavalry formations make their march, the scouts at the front lifting their torches high.

万火归一的士气，让历史的帷幕熊熊燃起。
The flames of glory burn bright, setting the curtain of history ablaze.

12TH-15 指尖的灰烬 / Dust Between Fingers

民兵营收容和治疗了不少在空袭中受伤的市民。用来替代病床的木板和伤者的呼痛塞满了几乎每个房间。
The militia camp is full of makeshift beds, sheltering the many civilians injured in the warlord's raid. The wails of pain echo in every corner.

即便如此，民兵们还是设法留出了一间“单人病房”。
Still, they've managed to set aside one private room.

梅蕾尔：……
Merel: ...

这是梅蕾尔第三十三次从椅子上站起来，绕着屋里唯一的病床检查伤者的情况。
Merel rises from her chair for the thirty-third time, pacing around the only bed in the room to check on the patient again.

尽管伤者的布帛下已经不再溢出“死亡”，她的视线还是无法好好停留在伤者身上。
The patient no longer oozes "death," yet she still can't bring herself to fully look at him.

她的眼神飘忽不定，一会儿落在地下室唯一的窗边，一会儿在椅面的木头纹路上停留。
Her gaze drifts aimlessly, toward the single basement window, the grain of the wooden chair.

她瞧见了布帛下摆边缘染上的巧克力渍。
A smudge of chocolate at the edge of the cloth catches her eye.

这是位没有体温的意识唤醒者，别列格勒漫长的秋季也没法融化一块坚实的巧克力。
This Awakened has an unnaturally low body temperature, so low that even in Bereggrad's long autumn, a piece of chocolate wouldn't melt.

梅蕾尔：……
Merel: ...

有人用了火吗？火能伤到卡戎吗？是否有人把她的朋友像烹制风肉一样架在了火上——
Could someone have used fire? Can fire even hurt Charon? Had her friend been turned over flames like a roast pig?

卡戎：梅蕾尔？
Charon: Merel?

梅蕾尔为自己的联想感到抱歉，但她的思维忍不住继续跳跃。
Merel feels guilty for the association, but in her franticness, her thoughts keep jumping around.

她无法自控地颤抖着，仿佛她自己就是点火的人——
A shiver runs through her, as if her own hand had struck the match to the kindling.

卡戎：……梅蕾尔？
Charon: Merel?

梅蕾尔：啊……啊！
Merel: Ah, oh!

梅蕾尔：卡戎……你醒了！
Merel: Charon, you're awake!

她背过身抹去了眼边的泪水，而后才连忙凑到床边扶起了卡戎。
She turns her face, quickly wiping away a tear, then hurries to Charon's side to help him sit up.

梅蕾尔：你……要喝水吗？你感觉如何？我去给你拿止痛药——
Merel: H-How are you feeling? Are you thirsty? Are you in pain? I'll go get the painkillers.

收尸人迟缓地摇了摇头。
Charon shakes his head slowly.

他不需要水，安瓿瓶中的药液于他而言也与水无异。而绷带下的身体已经顺利地黏合在了一起。
He has no need for water, and the medicine in the ampoule makes no difference to him. Besides, the body beneath his bandages has almost healed.

梅蕾尔：对了，玛尔纱把你的兜帽剪开了。我给你找了块新的布，你感觉怎么样？
Merel: Oh, right, Marsha cut your cloak when she was patching you up. Here, I found a new one for you. Do you like it?

她迫不及待地想要用行动弥补卡戎。
Merel is desperate to do something, anything, for him.

卡戎：你不用为我做任何事，梅蕾尔。
Charon: That won't be needed, Merel.

卡戎：你并不亏欠我。
Charon: You owe nothing.

收尸人用来遮盖“死亡”的衣料轻轻浮动，密闭的室内像是起了一阵风，撞得梅蕾尔有些听不清对方的话。
The cloth covering the "death" beneath shifts as if a breeze has just disturbed the air in the sealed room, muffling Charon's next words.

梅蕾尔：不……我做错了事情的。
Merel: No. I owe you a lot. What I did was wrong.

她用一个简单的“不”否认了对方的话，也否定了自己。
Her "no" is both a denial of him and herself.

梅蕾尔：我是神秘学家，我是第一防线学校培养出来的神秘学家，我还接受过执夜队的训练，我还去南极执行过任务……我可以战斗的。
Merel: I'm an arcanist trained by the SPDM and the vigils. I even fought a little in Antarctica. I can fight, I can. But I didn't.

梅蕾尔：如果我没有跑，他们说不定就没法抓住你——我们原本可以一起逃出来。
Merel: We could've escaped together, if I hadn't run away.

一个可怕的念头抓住了她。
A horrifying thought grips her.

梅蕾尔：一起……我们本来就不该一起的……
Merel: I should never have forced you to take me with you in the first place.

梅蕾尔：如果不是我想从队伍里逃跑，你这时应该还在蒙佩，照料那些从坟墓上开出的花。
Merel: If I hadn't been so desperate to run off from the "XII," you'd still be tending flowers in the graveyard back in Montpaix, instead of ...

卡戎：……
Charon: ...

卡戎：西线的战事已经结束了，死亡终究会将我引向该去的地方。
Charon: Death's call had grown heavy in the East. The path forward was clear.

卡戎：只要格鲁托夫的恶行不得到制止，我本就会顺着河来到这片草原。这与你无关，梅蕾尔。
Charon: So long as Krutov's atrocities grew unchecked. This was inevitable.

收尸人试图安抚这位同行的旅伴。可她像一只出现裂痕的盅，已经难以再盛装惊惧的水。
He tries to comfort her, but she is like a cracked cup, no longer able to contain her emotions.

梅蕾尔：哦……那、那我去把安德烈森牵过来，它一定很想你……
Merel: I-I'll go get Andreas. I'm sure he's missed you a lot.

或许“逃避”本身就是修补伤痕的方式。
Perhaps escape is one way to heal wounds.

收尸人没有制止她。
Charon doesn't stop her.

家里最厚的被褥、上个冬天剩下的柴垛和留在故乡的人组成了掩体，堵住了别列格勒的街头巷尾。
The streets of Bereggrad are barricaded with quilts, leftover firewood, and by the people who have refused to leave the city.

掩体后不时传来妇人忧心忡忡的声音，谈论着被秋天藏起来的命运，也谈起了或在远方、或在城外的家人们。
Women speak in low, anxious voices about what will come of this unusually warm autumn and about family who are now far away.

梅蕾尔：我记得马厩应该就在这附近……
Merel: Hmm. I'm pretty sure the stable's around here.

佳琳娜夫人：小姑娘，小姑娘。
Galina: Young lady. Young lady.

轻柔而苍老的呼唤吸引了梅蕾尔的注意，她左顾右盼看了一会儿，才发现一位坐在街边阴影里的老妇人。
The tender sound of an old voice draws Merel's attention. She turns to find an elderly lady sitting in the shade beside the road.

梅蕾尔：您叫我？
Merel: Um, are you talking to me?

佳琳娜夫人：我在红柳树村见过你，谢尔盖那几个小子说你是他们从河里捞起来的。
Galina: Yes, young lady. You were in Tamarovka, yes? Sergey said you were the "fish" he and his friends caught from the river.

梅蕾尔：多亏了他们，不然我恐怕就要被冲进海里喂鱼了。
Merel: Heh. If it weren't for them, I probably would've wound up in the stomach of some big fish.

梅蕾尔：说起来，骑兵军已经出征了吧？
Merel: Speaking of which, the soldiers have left already, right?

佳琳娜夫人：原来你也不知道。
Galina: Ah, so you don't know either.

老妇人的神色变得有些低落。
The lady's face falls.

佳琳娜夫人：我见你和基金会的人走了，以为你会知道得更清楚些。
Galina: I saw you with those Foundation people. I thought you'd have some news from the inside.

佳琳娜夫人：伊万只是派人劝我不要再待在村里，叫我到别列格勒来，和民兵、骑士还有基金会的人待一块儿，他说这样更安全，等他回来后就带我回芝诺总部。
Galina: *sigh* Ivan sent his men to bring me to Bereggrad. He told me it would be safer there under the protection of the militia and the Foundation. He promised to take me to Zeno headquarters once he's back.

梅蕾尔：伊万……伊万·伊万诺维奇？您是芝诺骑兵军军长的母亲？
Merel: Ivan? Wait, you don't mean Ivan Ivanovich, do you? You're his mother?

佳琳娜夫人：孩子也不会把所有事都告诉母亲。他们总有自己的顾虑，我早就习惯啦。
Galina: I am, dear. Though a child doesn't tell his mother everything, I'm sure he has his reasons. I've grown quite used to it.

佳琳娜夫人：有时他会神秘兮兮地派人把我接去总部。每到这时候我就知道，我好不容易关系熟络起来的邻居、屋前千辛万苦才栽活的红石竹马上就要消失了。
Galina: But, every time he suggests taking me to headquarters, I feel sad for the friends I made in the village and the red carnations in my little garden that soon they'll all vanish.

老妇人带着几分忧郁的坦白，让梅蕾尔心中一个角落蓦地塌陷了下去。
The old lady's sorrowful words make something inside Merel give way.

佳琳娜夫人：小姑娘，我们是不是又要去下一个时代啦？
Galina: Young lady, tell me, are we heading into another era?

梅蕾尔：……！
Merel: ...!

梅蕾尔紧张地捏着腰间的皮带，她歪着头，不敢看佳琳娜夫人的眼睛。
Merel nervously clutches the belt at her waist. She tilts her head, avoiding Ms. Galina's watery eyes.

梅蕾尔：对、对不起，夫人……我不知道您在说什么。
Merel: I'm sorry. I don't know what you're talking about.

佳琳娜夫人：别紧张，小姑娘。突然对你说了这么冒昧的话，要说对不起的该是我才对。
Galina: No, no, I should apologize, young lady, not you. I shouldn't be saying such things.

老妇人温和地捧起了梅蕾尔颤抖的手。
The old lady gently takes Merel's shaking hands in her own.

佳琳娜夫人：我老糊涂了，有时候自己都不知道自己在说什么。
Galina: I'm just an old woman. Sometimes I don't even know what I'm saying myself.

佳琳娜夫人：别闷闷不乐的了，来，年轻人就该笑笑。
Galina: Come now. Lift your chin and smile, young lady.

梅蕾尔：……
Merel: ...

梅蕾尔：夫人，您觉得我们现在的生活是有意义的吗？
Merel: Do you think there's still meaning in this kind of life?

梅蕾尔：即便您知道，您现在所做的一切都会像灰一样被风吹散，凭您自己的努力，无论如何都抓不住。
Merel: It's like I'm trying to catch something, but no matter how hard I try to hold onto it, everything I do, every friendship I make, will just be blown away, like dust.

佳琳娜夫人：哦……
Galina: Well ...

佳琳娜夫人了然地点了点头，扶着梅蕾尔在路边坐下。
Ms. Galina gives the kind of nod only someone with many years behind them can give and guides Merel to sit beside her.

佳琳娜夫人：伊万找到我的时候，我正坐在基辅大街的咖啡馆里，和朋友一起观看“礼炮6号”空间站的发射转播。
Galina: I was in a coffeehouse in Khreshchatyk, Kyiv, watching the Salyut 6 space station launch.

佳琳娜夫人：街边的乐队在为六十周年纪念日的演出排练《节日序曲》，曲子进入呈示部的时候，伊万扒开踢正步的仪仗队列，直接朝我冲了过来。
Galina: There was a marching band outside rehearsing Праздничная увертюра—the Festive Overture. As the piece moved into the exposition, I saw Ivan push aside the drum major and run straight toward me.

佳琳娜夫人：天哪，那一天他差点把咖啡馆的玻璃门撞碎。
Galina: God! He barged into that coffeehouse so fast that he nearly shattered the door.

佳琳娜夫人：然后，他张口就喊：“妈妈！”
Galina: And the first word from his mouth was "Mama!"

佳琳娜夫人短促地笑了一声。
Ms. Galina breaks into a soft laugh.

梅蕾尔：您……那时相信军长说的话吗？
Merel: So, did you believe him? That he was your son?

佳琳娜夫人的笑意在脸上扩大，眼角的皱纹深深挤在了一起。
Her smile grows, and deeper lines appear at the corners of her eyes.

佳琳娜夫人：信？我为此报了三次警，亲爱的！
Galina: Did I believe him? I called the police three times.

佳琳娜夫人：第一次，我说他骚扰，第二次，我觉得他是诈骗。
Galina: The first time, I told them I was being harassed. The second time, that he was a scammer.

梅蕾尔：第三次呢？
Merel: What about the third time?

佳琳娜夫人：第三次，我说他是个危险的时间错乱者，需要伟大祖国的强制收容！
Galina: The third time, I told them Ivan was a lunatic who claimed to be a time-traveler and should be committed to a sanitarium.

佳琳娜夫人：可每一次，都有芝诺或者基金会的老爷把他捞出来。
Galina: But, every time, he was quickly bailed out by Zeno or the Foundation.

佳琳娜夫人：他就在我的公寓楼下蹲着，抱着个破铁皮盒子，说里面是“我”的遗物——那个固执的小混蛋！我可还好好地活着呢。
Galina: He'd loiter around my building, holding a rusty tin box he claimed held "legacy items" I left behind. The nerve of that boy! I was still alive and well!

梅蕾尔：那个盒子里面……都有些什么？
Merel: What was in it? Did you see?

佳琳娜夫人：半块烤曲奇，还有一张我和他的合照，清晰得不像我们那个年代的产物。
Galina: Half a homemade cookie and a photo of the two of us. A photo so clear that it couldn't possibly have been produced in my time.

佳琳娜夫人：他花了半个秋天留在基辅，每天就在各种地方堵我。
Galina: He spent months following me to all sorts of places around Kyiv.

佳琳娜夫人：在公寓楼下，他说他小时候，我最喜欢在窗台上种红石竹，但一盆都没开过花。
Galina: One day, outside my building, he told me how I planted red carnations on the windowsill at his childhood home, but none ever bloomed.

佳琳娜夫人：我去裁缝店，他就说以前只要衣服掉了扣子，就会寄回家给我补，而我总会给他补上两颗有鸢尾花的扣子。
Galina: At the tailor's, he said that whenever a button fell off his clothes, he'd send it home for me to mend, and I would sew two buttons with irises on them.

佳琳娜夫人慢悠悠地说着，叙述的主语逐渐与自己重合，灰蓝的眼眸也慢慢盛满了难以言喻的情绪。
She speaks slowly, the story she tells gradually becoming her own. Her eyes are filled with wordless emotion.

佳琳娜夫人：那些场景我从未经历过，但后来却渐渐变得比冬天的骨头缝要更疼。
Galina: I didn't share those memories, but over time, I grew attached to them all the same. Now, when I think of them, there's a bittersweet pricking in my bones.

她俯身从地上抓起一把灰，放在梅蕾尔摊开的手掌上。
She leans down, gathers a handful of dust from the ground, and lets it fall into Merel's open palm.

佳琳娜夫人：你看，小姑娘，风确实会吹走灰烬。
Galina: You see, young lady. The wind does blow away the dust.

她引着梅蕾尔张开了五指。
She helps Merel spread her fingers.

佳琳娜夫人：你感觉到了什么？
Galina: But focus. Do you feel anything?

梅蕾尔：它……在溜走，在离开我。像一个时代的命中注定。
Merel: I feel it slipping away, leaving me behind, as if it's destined to happen.

佳琳娜夫人：没错，你“感觉”到了。
Galina: Exactly, you felt it.

佳琳娜夫人：咖啡馆里，空间站升空时我心跳的加速；《节日序曲》里小号嘹亮的一瞬带给我的振奋；伊万讲述“母亲”时我胸口里撕裂般的、不属于我的疼痛。
Galina: The excitement as the rocket soared into the sky, the surge of inspiration from the trumpet's cry in the Festive Overture, the heartbreaking ache in my chest as Ivan spoke to me of his mother ...

佳琳娜夫人：那无数个时刻的“感觉”，真切地留了下来。
Galina: These fleeting moments ... I felt them and imprinted them deep into my heart.

梅蕾尔：……
Merel: ...

梅蕾尔：所以……我们现在生活的意义并不在于“留下”什么，而是这个过程中我们“感觉”到了什么吗？
Merel: So then, the meaning of all this isn't in what we leave behind, but in what we feel as we go through it?

佳琳娜夫人：意义是过程本身燃烧的光和热，不是燃烧后能被记住多久的灰烬。
Galina: A spark lives for its light and warmth, not for the ashes it will leave behind. Don't you agree?

佳琳娜夫人：你叫什么名字，孩子？
Galina: What's your name, child?

梅蕾尔：梅蕾尔……梅蕾尔·范德维尔。
Merel: Merel. Merel Van der Veer.

佳琳娜夫人：记住了，梅蕾尔。既然注定要被风吹散，不如在燃烧的时候，烧得更亮些，把光和热，把那些真实的触感——温暖的、疼痛的、刺痒的、芳香的——
Galina: My dear Merel, every one of us is destined to return to dust, so why not feel as deeply as we can while we have the chance? Feel every one of our memories, bitter and sweet.

佳琳娜夫人：狠狠刻进这该死的、混乱的世界里，让这些“感觉”成为你的闪光。哪怕你真的因“暴雨”而消失，也会有属于你的“伊万”铭记你，找到你。
Galina: Savor and cherish each sparkling moment, even if the "Storm" washes you away one day. Because, even if you no longer feel them, someone like my Ivan will.

佳琳娜夫人先站了起来。
She stands.

梅蕾尔：夫人，您要去哪儿？
Merel: Where are you going?

佳琳娜夫人：去看看能帮上什么忙——去给这个时代留下些烙印。
Galina: To see what help I can offer, and to create more memories of this time before it's gone.

梅蕾尔看着她的背影逐渐消失在掩体后，矫健得不像一位古稀老人。
Merel watches her disappear behind a barricade. She moves with the strength of someone half her age.

她低下头，看着自己指间残留的沙砾。
And she looks down at the dust still trapped between her fingers.

12TH-16 怜悯之心 / Mercy

民兵：真看不出来，你挺会驯马的。
Militiaman: You seem to know a thing or two about training horses. Impressive.

民兵：现在城里有些小孩都不乐意往这儿来了，嫌马厩味道大……臭小鬼们，把哥萨克的立身之本都忘了。
Militiaman: Kids these days don't appreciate riding like they used to, complaining that the stables stink. Ungrateful brats! Forgotten the foundation of Cossack life, if you ask me.

梅蕾尔正有一搭没一搭地给旅伴刷着身体。
Merel brushes her companion absentmindedly.

梅蕾尔：它是个好孩子，我认识它的时候它就这么乖了，和我半点关系都没有——
Merel: Oh, it's got nothing to do with me. He's been a good boy since I met him in—

安德烈森：咴。
Andreas: *neigh*

漂亮的旅伴垂下头，在她的颈窝处喷出湿热的鼻息。
Andreas lowers his head, breathing warm, wet air against her neck.

梅蕾尔：——安德烈森！
Merel: Hey! Watch it, Andreas!

梅蕾尔手忙脚乱地用手背擦掉脖子上湿漉漉的水，年轻的民兵哈哈大笑了起来。
Merel scrambles to wipe the damp spot with the back of her hand. The young militiaman laughs.

民兵：它认识你，而且很喜欢你，看来确实是你的马。真可惜，我还以为能看见它在战场上大放异彩的模样。
Militiaman: Hah. Look at him. He's your horse all right. Shame. Thought I'd get to see him shine on the battlefield.

民兵拍了拍安德烈森的脖子，把缰绳递给了梅蕾尔。
He pats Andreas on the neck and hands the reins to Merel.

民兵：趁我回心转意前，牵走它吧。
Militiaman: Well, take him away then, before I change my mind.

梅蕾尔点点头，郑重地接过缰绳。
Merel nods, leading Andreas away with a solemn air.

梅蕾尔：谢谢你一直照顾安德烈森。等事情结束了，我会来帮你收拾马厩的。
Merel: Thanks for taking care of him. I'll come clean up the stable for you once the battle's over.

民兵：行啊，如果到时候咱们都还活着的话。
Militiaman: Sure, if we're both alive by then.

民兵挥了挥手，示意她赶紧走。
The militiaman waves her off.

梅蕾尔：那我就先……
Merel: Alright, see you—

梅蕾尔：……！
Merel: ...!

撞进视野里的黑色军服让呼吸又乱了分寸。
A black uniform crashes into her field of vision.

民兵：还走不走？不走的话安德烈森可就留给——
Militiaman: You leaving, or what? You know I'm serious about taking Andreas to—

只想着开个玩笑的民兵手里被塞进了一截缰绳。
The militiaman had only meant it as a joke, but the reins are thrust into his hands regardless.

梅蕾尔：帮我再照顾一下它！
Merel: I'll be back in a minute!

梅蕾尔屏住了呼吸，把心跳含在嘴里，试图将自己的存在感削弱至最隐微。
Merel holds her breath in an attempt to slow her heartbeat. She can't be spotted.

梅蕾尔：那些黑色的军服……这里难道不是民兵的控制区吗？他们是从哪里潜入的？
Merel: Black uniforms. But how did they manage to sneak past the militia?

一部分细胞啸叫着逃离危险，另一部分理智却控制着双腿走向了他们的来处——尽管每一步都像在沼泽中行军般艰难。
One instinct screams at her to run. Another quieter urge pulls her toward the sound. Each step feels like wading through a swamp.

梅蕾尔：只是重塑之手的小兵而已，没事的……去确认一下城墙是不是缺了口子就好，我不是要去跟踪他们。
Merel: This is fine. You're fine. Just a few Manus soldiers. You don't have to follow them. Just go check if there's a breach in the barricades.

梅蕾尔：他们发现不了我，我就不会和他们打起来。大不了还可以再试试变形术……
Merel: You'll just slip past, easy. No need to fight. And if they spot you, just shapeshift your way out of it.

暗巷尽头的地面像洒过汽水，蒸发后残留的糖浆黏腻无比。
The ground at the end of the alley is tacky, as if soda had spilled and dried there.

每次抬起脚，鞋底都像从黏鼠板上撕下一样，拉出黏腻的丝线。
Her boots lift with a soft sticky sound with every step, like a mouse tenderly moving its way through an old glue trap.

？？？：你在这儿做什么？
???: What are you doing here?

梅蕾尔：——！
Merel: ...!

她猛地朝声音的方向转身，鼻子撞上一块坚硬的钢铁。疼痛令她整张脸都皱了起来。
She spins toward the voice, and her nose collides with something hard as iron. She scrunches her face.

梅蕾尔：天哪……我感觉像是撞上了一堵墙……你也太结实了，玛尔纱。
Merel: Ourgh. Anyone ever tell you you're built like a tank, Marsha?

骑士掏出一块浆洗得发白的旧手帕，接住了梅蕾尔向下淌的鼻血。
The knight pulls a faded, starched handkerchief from her pocket and presses it to Merel's bleeding nose.

玛尔纱：别乱动，血很快就能止住了。
Marsha: Hold still. The bleeding will stop soon.

玛尔纱：看马厩的民兵说你急匆匆地往这里跑，你来这里做什么？你不该陪着卡戎吗？
Marsha: The militiaman at the stable said you went this way in a hurry. What's wrong? Shouldn't you be with Charon?

梅蕾尔：卡戎已经醒了，我本来想通知你的……但有更重要的事！
Merel: I was going to tell you Charon was awake again, but something's happened.

梅蕾尔：我发现了重塑之手的士兵，眨眼就不见了——但他们是从这个巷子里走出去的！
Merel: Manus soldiers—they're here! They were gone in a flash, but I saw them go into that alley with my own eyes!

梅蕾尔：我怕街垒的防线破了口子什么的，想来检查一下。
Merel: That's why I came here, to check if there's something wrong with the fortifications.

玛尔纱：重塑之手？不是普通匪军？
Marsha: You're sure it was the Manus, not bandits?

梅蕾尔：一定是他们，我见过很多次那种黑色的制服，不会认错。
Merel: Absolutely! There's no way I'd mistake those uniforms.

玛尔纱：……还好你没有贸然跟过去，这太危险了。怎么这个时候胆子这么大了？
Marsha: This is bad. Good thing you didn't do anything reckless. But what you were doing is more than dangerous enough, don't you think?

梅蕾尔搓着鼻子，不知怎么回话。骑士拍拍她的脑袋，端详起这一段疑似有重塑士兵活动的小路。
Merel just rubs her nose. Marsha pats her head, then scans the narrow alley Merel pointed out.

玛尔纱：小路尽头的出口是被临时修建的砖墙堵死的，两旁建筑的窗户也好好地锁上……这是一条死路。
Marsha: That alley? But the exit has been sealed off. The militia even made sure the windows on the sides were locked tight. It's a dead end.

脚下碾碎的苔藓与地衣，在城市里确实不常见，但在这久无人迹之处，生命自会倔强地蔓延。
Crushed moss and lichen lie underfoot—a rarity in the city, but in forgotten corners like this, life will find a way.

一小截纱布落在潮湿的墙角。
A scrap of gauze lies in a damp corner.

玛尔纱：……嗯？
Marsha: Hmm?

玛尔纱：蓝黑相间的液体，像是从他们的面具上流下来的。除此之外，还有……血液。
Marsha: This blue-black liquid ... I think I've seen it seeping from their masks before. And there's blood.

玛尔纱：氧化得不算严重，但出血量很大。也许是受伤的重塑之手士兵用过的绷带。
Marsha: Slightly oxidized, but the loss looks heavy. Some of them must be seriously injured.

玛尔纱：可纱布上还残留了一些石炭酸的气味，重塑之手通常不会用它来处理伤口，他们更青睐草药……
Marsha: Hmm, smells like carbolic acid. Unusual for the Manus to use it on wounds. They prefer natural salves.

玛尔纱：只有城里的医院才会用这种消毒剂，也就是说……糟了，重塑之手的人去过医院！
Marsha: You can usually only find disinfectants like this in large medical facilities. Wait. They must have been to one recently!

梅蕾尔：医院？……可他们是怎么混进来的？
Merel: What? But, how?

玛尔纱：重塑之手也许有他们的办法，但现在我们没有时间追究这个。
Marsha: They must have used some trick to get in unnoticed, but there's little point in dwelling on it now.

玛尔纱：我方占领区内有两家大医院，最近的是波克罗夫儿童医院，以及两条街外的神圣第七疗养院。
Marsha: There are two big medical facilities in this district: the nearest one, Pokrov Children's Hospital, and the Sanatorium two streets down from here.

玛尔纱：梅蕾尔，你快去通知民兵和伊戈尔的人往这两个地方加派人手，重塑之手可能还有人留在医院内。
Marsha: Merel, I need you to tell the militia and the Gryphons to send men to both locations. The Manus soldiers you saw could be hiding there.

梅蕾尔：好的，那你呢？
Merel: Understood. What about you?

玛尔纱：我先去查看儿童医院的情况，那里全是孩子，面对敌人根本没有抵抗能力。
Marsha: I'll go check on the kids at the children's hospital. I have to make sure they're safe.

玻璃碎了，风挤着钻进来，把手上打着石膏、头上绑着纱布的孩子们逼到了墙角。
By a shattered window, a nurse shelters a group of children huddled in a corner, their arms in plaster and their heads bandaged.

护士：你们要干什么？！你们已经把药全拿走了，为什么还要揪着几个孩子不放？
Nurse: Why won't you let the children go? You've already taken all the medicine. What more do you want from them?

重塑军官：我耐心地向你解释过，人类，把医院里的神秘学家后代交出来，我要带他们回到自己真正的家庭。
Manus Officer: Tsk. Didn't I already explain this to you, human? I'm bringing the newest generation of arcanists back to their rightful home.

护士：你们需要人质，把我带走就好了！
Nurse: If it's a hostage you want, take me instead!

她大张着双臂，让自己矮瘦的身躯成为盖住这些孩子的伞。她鼻梁上青了一块，嘴角也破了，但眼神依然冷静。
She spreads her slender arms wide behind her, like an umbrella over the children. Her nose is bruised and her lip is split, but her eyes are steady.

重塑军官：你得不到救赎，我们的队伍也不欢迎你，人类。
Manus Officer: You're not worthy of even that, human filth.

军官举起枪，狠狠地砸向她的头，逼她跪下。
The officer lifts his gun and smashes it down on her head in an attempt to force her to her knees.

护士踉跄了一步，但是没有倒下。
The nurse staggers but stays on her feet.

护士：……我教孩子们认字，而不是教他们认命。
Nurse: Then I won't yield to you, and neither will my children!

护士：记住了，我们的骑兵会把你们这些可鄙的侵略者都赶出去！！
Nurse: Soon, the riders will come and crush all you invaders!

军官挥挥手，一个头戴面具的士兵便上前想要拽住一个孩子的胳膊。
The officer signals. A masked soldier moves to grab a child.

护士：别碰他！！
Nurse: Don't you dare touch him!

护士扑了过去，猛地把士兵撞倒在了地上。
The nurse throws herself forward, knocking the soldier down.

一拳，又一拳。哪怕挥舞的拳头已经皮开肉绽，士兵脸上的面具也被打落，她始终没有停下。
She lands blow after blow. Even when her fists are raw and split, even when his mask slips off, she keeps fighting.

她全然没有发现已经上膛的手枪对准了她的后脑勺。
She doesn't see the pistol aimed at the back of her head.

女孩：娜斯佳小姐！
Girl: Nastya!

她在枪响与尖叫声中倒在孩子们身前。
The shot and the children's cries echo as one as she falls to the ground in front of them.

玛尔纱抹掉眼角无用的汗液与泪水，握紧堑壕棒，紧紧地贴在柱子后的阴影里。
Marsha wipes away the useless sweat and tears from the corners of her eyes, grips her trench club, and presses herself into the shadow of a pillar.

玛尔纱：重塑之手真的在这里。
Marsha: Manus Vindictae ... They're really here.

玛尔纱：其他房间都空了，医院的成年人……都不在了，剩下的孩子都聚在这里。
Marsha: No signs of children in other rooms, and the adults are all gone. The Manus must have gathered every child they could find in here.

黑衣士兵分头四散在走廊里，踢开每一扇门，在离开之前抢走哪怕是消毒棉球这样的小东西。
The soldiers in black spread through the hall, kicking down doors and taking even the smallest of supplies.

只有领头军官一个人用枪压制住了几个孩子，正向她的方向走来。
Only one officer stays, his gun still trained on the group of children as he moves toward Marsha's hiding place.

玛尔纱：和在乡村做的事一样，重塑之手一直在掳掠神秘学家，连孩子也不放过……
Marsha: They have been abducting arcanists from the villages, but to think they'd even lay hands on children.

玛尔纱：还有十步。
Marsha: Alright, ten steps away from me.

玛尔纱：五步，四步，三步……
Marsha: Five, four, three ...

“砰——！”
*thud*

骑士从阴影中一步踏出，沉重的钝器在重塑之手军官身上敲出一声干净利落的闷响。
She lands a heavy, blunt strike cleanly on the Manus officer's skull.

男孩：——你、你是谁？！
Boy: Wh-Who are you?

玛尔纱：别怕，我是其他医院过来的医生。我会带你们去安全的地方，但是要听我的话去做，好吗？
Marsha: Don't worry, little ones. I'm a doctor from another hospital. I'll take you to safety. Just stay close to me, and follow my instructions, and we will get through this together, alright?

也许是身上消毒水的味道起了作用，长期和医生待在一起的孩子们停止了怀疑，选择相信这个熟悉的气味。
Maybe it's the smell of disinfectant she carries, or that they're accustomed to following a doctor's instructions, the children trust her quickly.

男孩：唔……
Boy: Alright.

重塑士兵：喂，长官那边怎么没动静了？你和我过去看看。
Manus Soldier: Hey, it's gotten a little quiet, don't you think? We should go check on the boss.

几个在不远处搜查的士兵发现了异常，他们端着武器，朝着长官倒下的方向寻了过来。
The soldiers halt their search, turning with weapons raised toward their fallen officer.

玛尔纱：来吧，快进去！
Marsha: Come. Get inside!

玛尔纱俯下身，推着恐慌的孩子们躲入了楼梯后一间小小的仓库。她最后一个跨入门内，关门时嘈杂的脚步已经靠得很近了。
Marsha crouches down and guides the frightened children into a small storeroom behind the stairs. She slips in last, swiftly closing the door as footsteps approach.

女孩：娜斯佳小姐会没事吗？
Girl: Will Nastya be okay?

玛尔纱没有办法回答这个问题。她脱下披风，盖在孩子们头上。
Marsha has no answer to this question. She takes off her cloak and drapes it over the children's heads.

玛尔纱：我要你们在房间里藏一会儿，之后听见什么声音，都不要出声。像是在玩捉迷藏一样。知道吗？
Marsha: I need you to stay here in this room and be completely quiet no matter what happens. Like a game of hide-and-seek, easy. Can you do that?

女孩：嗯……嗯。
Girl: Y-Yes.

她一边安抚着发抖的孩子们，一边压低呼吸，逐渐平复猛烈的心跳。
She rubs their shoulders through the cloak and slows her breathing to steady her own racing heart.

紧绷的神经逐渐被神秘术抚平，她的注意力得以再次放在眼前的局势上。
Her arcane skill smooths her frayed nerves, returning her focus.

玛尔纱：医院里不知道还有多少敌人，友军应该很快就会来了。在这之前，守住这个房间应该是最好的方法。
Marsha: Merel will bring help soon, but there's no telling how many Manus are here. The best course of action is to hold this room.

重塑士兵：你在房间里吗，长官？
Manus Soldier: Are you in there, sir?

重塑士兵：我们该走了，芝诺和民兵团的人应该快要发现我们在这儿了——长官？！
Manus Soldier: We'd better get going before Zeno and the militia find—huh? Sir? Sir?!

在走廊的阴影中，士兵发现自己的上级俯身倒在地上。
In the shadows, the soldier finds his commander on the floor.

重塑士兵：该死的，他被袭击了！那些小杂种肯定藏在门里！
Manus Soldier: Damn it! Those little brats knocked him out! They can't have gotten far. Search the room!

士兵们意识到了这扇敲不开的门后有他们想要的东西。
It doesn't take long for them to find the sealed door.

重塑士兵：把所有人都叫过来，把门砸开，术士想要的那些小崽子肯定在里面！
Manus Soldier: Door's locked. Call everyone over; we'll smash it open and drag those brats to the ritualist!

玛尔纱：……！
Marsha: ...!

门板承受了一次重击，白蜡木板材碎裂的声音与急躁的呼喊一同响起。
The door shudders under a heavy blow. The sound of cracking white ash wood splinters among frantic shouts.

男孩：姐、姐姐……
Boy: Ms. Doctor, I ... I ...

玛尔纱：嘘……不要大声说话，还记得我刚才是怎么说的吗？有坏人在外面找你们，你们就要像玩捉迷藏一样躲好。
Marsha: Shhh. Keep your voice down. We're playing hide-and-seek, remember? We can't get caught by the baddies.

女孩：可、可是，我害怕……娜斯佳小姐，他们把她……
Girl: B-But I'm scared. And Nastya ...

玛尔纱：嘿，你们听过骑士的故事吗？
Marsha: Hey, have you ever heard any stories about knights?

男孩：我爸爸给我讲过伊利亚的故事，他是一个非常厉害的哥萨克。
Boy: Well, Papa once told me the story of a legendary Cossack called Ilya.

女孩：我还记得，哥哥从莫斯科带回一本书，里面写了十二个骑士的故事，是哥哥念给我听的……
Girl: My brother brought home a book from Moscow. It had twelve knights in it.

玛尔纱：这都是很棒的故事，不过，我要说的是一个你们所有人都从来没有听过的故事。
Marsha: I'm sure both stories are wonderful. But I have a story about knights to share as well, and I bet none of you have ever heard it.

男孩：那是一个什么样的故事？
Boy: What happens in it?

玛尔纱：如果你们能好好待在房间里，不要乱跑，我会回来把故事讲完。答应我，好吗？
Marsha: It's a wonderful story too. But you need to promise me you'll stay in this room, and I'll be back soon to tell you all about it. Deal?

男孩：那……那好。你要出去吗，姐姐？你要去哪里，真的还会回来吗？
Boy: Deal. But where are you going, Ms. Doctor? You'll come back soon, won't you?

玛尔纱：当然会回来，这不是我们已经说好的吗？
Marsha: Of course I will! A promise is a promise.

玛尔纱：你们只要乖乖地……等我回来。
Marsha: Just be good, every one of you, and wait for me here.

在下一次撞击来临的前一刻，她推门而出，又迅速地将身后的门给关上。
Before the next strike comes, she flings the door open and quickly closes it behind her.

在遥远的山间，住着一群神秘的骑士，他们在高山修道院的严寒中过着清苦而隐秘的生活。
In a secluded monastery perched atop a high, snowy mountain lived a group of mysterious knights.

他们的剑是雪原中铸成的秘宝，盔甲上总是覆盖着细密的白雪——
Their swords glittered like gleaming silver when they fought across the frozen fields, their helmets and pauldrons coated in dazzling white frost.

有一年冬天，落雪比以往任何时候都多，郊区的山谷中堆满了能让人深深陷进去的积雪。
One winter, the snow fell heavier than ever before, burying every path in the valley beneath a thick white blanket.

一个小女孩在雪地中迷了路。她走了几乎一整夜，都看不见任何一户人家。
Amidst the snow, a little girl had lost her way. She wandered all night seeking help and shelter, but all she found was the endless white around her.

清晨来临时，她倒在地上，在厚厚的雪中摔出一个小小的坑。
At sunrise, having used every last ounce of her strength, she collapsed, leaving a small hollow in the snow.

在她快要睡着的时候，远远地看见一道白晃晃的影子，比那彻骨的风雪还要洁白……
Just before she froze into a little popsicle, a figure appeared, gleaming even brighter than the pale landscape.

白衣骑士：这是……一个女孩？
Knight in White: What's this? A girl?

迷路的女孩：……
Disoriented Girl: ...

白衣骑士：仁慈的主，我差点以为是一只狐狸，还好过来多看了一眼。
Knight in White: O merciful Lord, I thought it only a stray fox.

白衣骑士：看来下山的行程要取消了——拉住我的手，可怜的孩子，靠到我背上来，我带你到修道院里吃点东西。
Knight in White: It seems my trip to the valley must be delayed. Come, child, lean on my back and hold my hands. I shall take you back to the monastery and get something warm in your belly.

白衣骑士：放心，我绝不会让你死在这儿的。
Knight in White: Worry not. I shan't have you die on me.

……迷路的女孩和骑士一同回到了修道院——那是一座矗立在峭壁上的坚固城堡，就连邪恶的巨龙也不敢接近。
Thanks to this kindhearted knight, the girl survived. To her, the monastery, which nursed her back to health, seemed like an impregnable fortress that even dragons dared not approach.

女孩在这座城堡中长大了，她在漫长的训练后如愿以偿地成为了骑士，就像那个在冬天拯救她的人一样。
After years of training, the little girl grew to become a capable knight, just like her rescuer that winter night.

但是战争……
But then, war ...

玛尔纱：……战争随之而来，她也和其他骑士一样应征走向战场。他们杀死了数不清的敌人，心中的疑虑也越来越多。
Marsha: War found its way to their once secluded fortress, and she, along with her fellow knights, was called to the battlefield, forced to fight. And after taking one life after another, doubts began to grow in their hearts.

玛尔纱：皇帝在宫殿里说，骑士的修行就是磨炼杀人的技艺。但骑士们知道，这场战争将他们的尊严踩在了脚下。
Marsha: They were welcomed to the glamorous halls of the royal palace and praised for their skills, their slaughter. But for these noble knights, those words were not praise. No, they were wounds to their dignity and honor.

玛尔纱：我们挥舞着战旗，手持长剑，却……从来不是……
Marsha: We were fighters, yes. We raised banners and wielded swords, but we weren't ...

从来不是为了杀戮而战。
We were never meant to kill.

梅蕾尔：我听见声音了，就在门后面……玛尔纱？是你在说话吗？
Merel: I hear someone, in that room. Marsha? Is that you?

托勒密：过来，我们一起把门撞开就知道了。
Ptolemy: We'll know once we blast this damn door down. Come on, men!

民兵：三、二、一！用力撞！
Militiaman: Three, two, one, push!

梅蕾尔：天、天呐，玛尔纱……还有这么多孩子——快来人帮帮忙！她伤得好重！
